Book of Hajj. Ashraf al-Hidaya Urdu commentary on Hidaya volume three. And the time of Tawaf al-Sadr is before departing from Makkah. And if he leaves three circuits of Tawaf al-Sadr, then sadaqah is obligatory upon him, i.e., for each circuit he gives half a sa' of wheat.

1
Sahib al-Quduri said: If a muhrim performed an obligatory tawaf inside the [space of] the Hijr. Tawaf inside the Hijr means that he goes around the Kaaba and enters the open space between the Kaaba and the wall, i.e., the Hatim is omitted from the circuits and he circumambulates inside the Hatim. So if this person is present in Makkah, he should repeat this tawaf because the tawaf is obligatory from outside the Hatim, and he did not do tawaf from outside the Hatim; therefore it will be said that he did not perform the prescribed tawaf. So to perform it in the prescribed manner, he should repeat the entire tawaf. If he repeats the missed tawaf, nothing is incumbent upon him.

And if he repeats specifically over the Hijr, it suffices him, because he has made up what is prescribed. And it is that he starts from his right side outside the Hijr until he reaches its end, then enters the Hijr from the opening and exits from the other side; he does this seven times. If he returns to his family and did not repeat it, then a dam is obligatory upon him because a deficiency occurred in his tawaf by leaving what is close to a quarter, so sadaqah does not suffice him.

Explanation: The person who omitted the tawaf of the open space between the Hatim and the Kaaba (called the Hijr), if he only repeats the tawaf of the Hijr, it is permissible because he has made up what he missed. Sahib al-Hidaya says: The repetition of the tawaf of the Hijr is that he starts from the right side outside the Hijr until he reaches the end of the Hijr, then enters the Hijr from the opening and exits from the other side. This is one circuit; he does this seven times. And if this person returns to his homeland and does not repeat the tawaf of the Hatim, then a dam is obligatory upon him because a deficiency occurred in his tawaf by leaving close to a quarter. Therefore sadaqah is not sufficient for its compensation, rather a dam is obligatory.

Tawaf al-Ziyarah without wudu and Tawaf al-Sadr in the last days of Tashriq while pure: then one dam. And if he performed Tawaf al-Ziyarah in a state of janabah, then two dams are necessary.

And whoever performed Tawaf al-Ziyarah without wudu and Tawaf al-Sadr in the last days of Tashriq while pure, then upon him is one dam. If he performed Tawaf al-Ziyarah while junub, then upon him are two dams according to Abu Hanifa, and they (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said upon him is one dam, because in the first case, Tawaf al-Sadr is not transferred to Tawaf al-Ziyarah because it is obligatory, and repeating Tawaf al-Ziyarah due to impurity is not obligatory, rather it is recommended, so it is not transferred to it. And in the second case, Tawaf al-Sadr is transferred to Tawaf al-Ziyarah because it (Tawaf al-Ziyarah) is deserving of repetition, so it becomes like Tawaf al-Sadr, delaying Tawaf al-Ziyarah from the days of Nahr. So the dam is obligatory for leaving al-Sadr by agreement, and for delaying the latter, there is a difference. However, he is commanded to repeat Tawaf al-Sadr as long as he is in Makkah, and he is not commanded after returning, as we have explained.

Translation: And whoever performed Tawaf al-Ziyarah without wudu and Tawaf al-Sadr in the last days of Tashriq with wudu, then upon him is one dam. And if he performed Tawaf al-Ziyarah in a state of janabah, then according to Imam Abu Hanifa two dams are obligatory, and the Sahibayn said that one dam is obligatory upon him. Because in the first case, Tawaf al-Sadr is not transferred to Tawaf al-Ziyarah, because Tawaf al-Sadr is obligatory and repeating Tawaf al-Ziyarah due to minor impurity is not obligatory but recommended. Therefore Tawaf al-Sadr will not be transferred to Tawaf al-Ziyarah. And in the second case, due to leaving Tawaf al-Sadr, a dam is obligatory by consensus, and due to delaying Tawaf al-Ziyarah, it is obligatory with difference of opinion. However, as long as he is in Makkah, he is commanded to repeat Tawaf al-Sadr, and after returning to his homeland, he is not commanded, as we have stated.

Explanation: In this passage, two issues are mentioned. First: A person performed Tawaf al-Ziyarah without wudu and Tawaf al-Sadr with wudu at the end of the days of Tashriq, then upon him, by consensus, one dam is obligatory. Second: He performed Tawaf al-Ziyarah in a state of janabah and Tawaf al-Sadr with purity at the end of the days of Tashriq, then in this case, according to Abu Hanifa two dams, and according to the Sahibayn one dam is obligatory. The reason for the difference between these two issues is that in the first case, Tawaf al-Sadr will not be transferred to Tawaf al-Ziyarah because Tawaf al-Sadr is obligatory and repeating Tawaf al-Ziyarah due to minor impurity is not obligatory but recommended. Therefore there is no need to transfer Tawaf al-Sadr to Tawaf al-Ziyarah; rather Tawaf al-Ziyarah remains in its place and Tawaf al-Sadr remains in its place, but one dam becomes obligatory for performing Tawaf al-Ziyarah without wudu. And in the second case, when he performed Tawaf al-Ziyarah in a state of janabah, Tawaf al-Sadr will be transferred to Tawaf al-Ziyarah, because Tawaf al-Ziyarah with janabah is like nothingness, so its repetition is obligatory. So when Tawaf al-Ziyarah with janabah is in the status of nothingness, then Tawaf al-Sadr which was performed at the end of the days of Tashriq will be transferred to it, and we will say that this is a repetition of Tawaf al-Ziyarah. Now this person becomes one who omitted Tawaf al-Sadr and delayed Tawaf al-Ziyarah from the days of Nahr. So one dam becomes obligatory due to leaving Tawaf al-Sadr, and there is consensus on this. And the second dam becomes obligatory due to delaying Tawaf al-Ziyarah. But this second dam is only obligatory according to Abu Hanifa, not according to the Sahibayn. Therefore in this case, according to Imam Abu Hanifa two dams are obligatory, and according to the Sahibayn only one dam is obligatory. However, it is necessary that in the second case, as long as this person is present in Makkah, he is commanded to repeat Tawaf al-Sadr, but after returning to his homeland, he is not commanded.
Source pages p. 439

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidaya discusses two distinct but related issues concerning tawaf. The first part, quoting Sahib al-Quduri, addresses the ruling if a pilgrim performs an obligatory tawaf inside the Hijr (the semicircular area between the Kaaba and the Hatim wall). The tawaf must be performed outside the Hatim; going inside nullifies the validity of that circuit. If the person is still in Makkah, he must repeat the entire tawaf in the prescribed manner. However, if he only repeats the circuits that missed going outside the Hijr by doing a specific pattern (starting outside, entering through the gap, exiting the other side) seven times, it suffices as compensation. If he returns home without making up the deficiency, he must offer a dam (sacrifice), because the deficiency is close to a quarter of the tawaf, and sadaqah (charity) is not sufficient.

The second part deals with the case where a person performs Tawaf al-Ziyarah (obligatory tawaf of Hajj) without wudu (minor impurity) or in a state of janabah (major impurity), and later performs Tawaf al-Sadr (farewell tawaf) in purity at the end of the days of Tashriq. The text presents the positions of Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). If Tawaf al-Ziyarah was without wudu and Tawaf al-Sadr was pure, there is consensus on one dam. If Tawaf al-Ziyarah was done while junub, then according to Abu Hanifa two dams are required, while the Sahibayn say only one. The reasoning is based on whether Tawaf al-Sadr can be transferred to count as a repeat of Tawaf al-Ziyarah. When the impurity is minor (no wudu), repeating Tawaf al-Ziyarah is recommended but not obligatory, so Tawaf al-Sadr remains separate. When the impurity is major (janabah), Tawaf al-Ziyarah is void and must be repeated; hence Tawaf al-Sadr is transferred to become its repetition. Consequently, the person is considered to have omitted Tawaf al-Sadr (consensus dam) and delayed Tawaf al-Ziyarah (disputed second dam). The passage also notes that if still in Makkah, he is ordered to repeat Tawaf al-Sadr, but not after returning home.

Key Terms
جنابة (janabah): State of major ritual impurity requiring ghusl (full bath), e.g., after sexual intercourse, menstruation, or childbirth.
حدث أصغر (hadath asghar): Minor impurity requiring wudu (ablution).
انتقال (intiqal): Transfer of the obligation of one tawaf to another; used here to describe Tawaf al-Sadr being counted as a repetition of the void Tawaf al-Ziyarah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Sahibayn, how many dams are required if a person performs Tawaf al-Ziyarah while junub and then performs Tawaf al-Sadr in purity?
A) One dam
B) Two dams
C) No dam
D) Sadaqah only

Key Takeaway
When Tawaf al-Ziyarah is performed while junub, Abu Hanifa requires two dams; the Sahibayn require one; the mufta bihi is one dam.

Hajj — Pilgrimage
intermediate
6 min
Transfer of Tawaf al-Sadr to Tawaf al-Ziyarah: The Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Dams
Intra-Hanafi dispute on transfer of Tawaf al-Sadr and number of dams

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on transferring Tawaf al-Sadr to compensate for Tawaf al-Ziyarah performed with impurity and state the number of dams required according to Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
Transfer of Tawaf al-Sadr depends on whether repeating Tawaf al-Ziyarah is wajib or mustahab.

This passage addresses an intra-Hanafi dispute about a pilgrim who performed Tawaf al-Ziyarah in a state of ritual impurity. The question is whether the later Tawaf al-Sadr can be 'transferred' to serve as a repetition of the deficient Tawaf al-Ziyarah. The answer determines how many dams (blood offerings) are required. We must distinguish between minor impurity (lack of wudu) and major impurity (janabah), as the ruling differs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two impurity scenarios
Note the two cases: (1) Tawaf al-Ziyarah performed without wudu (minor impurity), (2) Tawaf al-Ziyarah performed in janabah (major impurity). In both cases, the pilgrim later performs Tawaf al-Sadr with purity at the end of Tashriq days.
2
Understand the concept of 'transfer' (naql)
Transfer means that the later Tawaf al-Sadr is counted as the required repetition of the deficient Tawaf al-Ziyarah. This affects whether the pilgrim is considered to have missed Tawaf al-Sadr and/or delayed Tawaf al-Ziyarah.
3
Determine wajib vs mustahab repetition
After impurity, is repeating Tawaf al-Ziyarah wajib or mustahab? For minor impurity (without wudu), repetition is mustahab (recommended). For major impurity (janabah), repetition is wajib (obligatory) because the tawaf is invalid.
4
Apply the transfer rule
If repetition is mustahab, Tawaf al-Sadr is not transferred (it remains as a separate wajib). If repetition is wajib, Tawaf al-Sadr is transferred to count as the repetition of Tawaf al-Ziyarah.
This leads to different numbers of dams.
5
Calculate the number of dams
In scenario 1 (without wudu): No transfer, so one dam is due for leaving Tawaf al-Sadr (by consensus). In scenario 2 (janabah): Transfer occurs, so the pilgrim is considered to have missed Tawaf al-Sadr (one dam by consensus) and delayed Tawaf al-Ziyarah (one dam according to Abu Hanifa, but not according to the Sahibayn). Hence, Abu Hanifa requires two dams; the Sahibayn require one.

صاحبین کے نزدیک فقط ایک دم واجب ہوگا۔ ہاں اتنی بات ضرور ہے کہ دوسری صورت میں جب تک یہ شخص مکہ میں موجود سے اس کو طواف صدر کے اعادہ کا حکم کیا جائے گا لیکن وطن واپس آنے کے بعد یہ حکم نہیں کیا جائے گا۔
It is mustahab, so it is not transferred to it. And in the second case, Tawaf al-Sadr is transferred to Tawaf al-Ziyarah because it is entitled to repetition, so it becomes like a fire [?] delaying Tawaf al-Ziyarah from the days of Nahr. So the dam is obligatory for leaving Tawaf al-Sadr by consensus, and for delaying the other according to difference. Except that he is ordered to repeat Tawaf al-Sadr as long as he is in Makkah, and he is not ordered after returning, as we have explained.
Source pages p. 440

Commentary
This is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding a person who performed Tawaf al-Ziyarah without wudu (or in janabah) and later performed Tawaf al-Sadr with wudu at the end of Tashriq days. The text discusses whether Tawaf al-Sadr can be transferred to compensate for the deficient Tawaf al-Ziyarah. In the first case (without wudu), Tawaf al-Sadr is not transferred because the repetition of Tawaf al-Ziyarah is mustahab (recommended), not wajib, so one dam is due for missing Tawaf al-Sadr. In the second case (in janabah), Tawaf al-Sadr is transferred because the repetition of Tawaf al-Ziyarah is wajib (due to major impurity), so according to Imam Abu Hanifa, two dams are due: one for missing Tawaf al-Sadr (by consensus) and one for delaying Tawaf al-Ziyarah (by difference with the Sahibayn who hold only one dam). The text also notes that if the person is still in Makkah, he should repeat Tawaf al-Sadr; after returning home, he is not ordered to return.

Key Terms
طواف الصدر (Tawaf al-Sadr): The farewell tawaf performed before leaving Makkah, also called Tawaf al-Wada'.
طواف الزيارة (Tawaf al-Ziyarah): The essential tawaf performed on the 10th of Dhul Hijjah, also called Tawaf al-Ifadah.
حدث (hadath): Ritual impurity, here specifically hadath asghar (minor impurity like lack of wudu) and hadath akbar (major impurity like janabah).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, how many dams are required if a person performs Tawaf al-Ziyarah in a state of janabah and then performs Tawaf al-Sadr with wudu at the end of Tashriq?
A) One dam
B) Two dams
C) No dam
D) Three dams

Key Takeaway
The transfer of Tawaf al-Sadr hinges on whether repetition of Tawaf al-Ziyarah is wajib (major impurity) or mustahab (minor impurity), determining the number of dams: one or two.

Hajj — Pilgrimage
intermediate
6 min
Umrah Tawaf and Sa'y Without Wudu
Ruling on performing Umrah tawaf and sa'y without wudu and then becoming halal

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for a person who performs Umrah tawaf and sa'y without wudu, and explain the conditions under which repetition or a dam is required.

Core Idea
Tawaf without wudu is valid but deficient; repetition is wajib in Makkah, but if home, a dam is due only for tawaf – not for sa'y.

This lesson examines a common Umrah scenario: performing tawaf and sa'y without wudu. The Hanafi school offers a detailed ruling that distinguishes between the obligation to repeat while still in Makkah and the penalty if one has already returned home. By understanding the reasoning (talil) behind these rules, you will be able to apply them correctly and avoid common misconceptions about the role of purification in the Umrah rites.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its deficiency
The person performed tawaf and sa'y for Umrah without wudu, then became halal. The deficiency is in tawaf due to lack of purification; sa'y does not require wudu but follows tawaf.
2
Determine the remedy while in Makkah
Repeat both tawaf and sa'y. No penalty (dam) is required because the deficiency is removed by repetition.
The repetition of sa'y is because it is a follower (taba') of tawaf.
3
Analyze the scenario after returning home
If the person has returned home without repeating, a dam is due only for tawaf, not for sa'y. There is no obligation to return to Makkah.
The deficiency in tawaf is considered minor; the tahlul has occurred by performing the rukn.
4
Examine the reasoning (talil)
Wudu is a wajib in tawaf, not a condition of validity. Sa'y does not require wudu; its validity depends on following a valid tawaf. The correct view is that no dam is due for sa'y even if only tawaf is repeated.
Some scholars hold a dam for sa'y, but the Hanafi correct view (fi al-sahih) is no dam.

Source Text

وَمَنْ طَافَ لِعُمْرَتِهِ وَسَعَى عَلَى غَيْرِ وُضُوءٍ وَحَلَّ فَمَا دَامَ بِمَكَّةَ يُعِيدُهُمَا وَلَا شَيْءَ عَلَيْهِ أَمَّا إِعَادَةُ الطَّوَافِ فَلِتَمَكُّنِ النَّقْصِ فِيهِ بِسَبَبِ الْحَدَثِ وَأَمَّا السَّعَى فَلِأَنَّهُ تَبَعٌ لِلطَّوَافِ وَإِذَا أَعَادَهُمَا لَا شَيْءَ عَلَيْهِ لِارْتِفَاعِ النَّقْصِ وَإِنْ رَجَعَ إِلَى أَهْلِهِ قَبْلَ أَنْ يُعِيدَ فَعَلَيْهِ دَمٌ لِتَرْكِ الطَّهَارَةِ فِيهِ وَلَا يُؤْمَرُ بِالْعَوْدِ لِوُقُوعِ التَّحَلُّلِ بِأَدَاءِ الرُّكْنِ إِذِ النَّقْصُ يَسِيرٌ وَلَيْسَ عَلَيْهِ فِي السَّعْيِ شَيْءٌ لِأَنَّهُ أَتَى بِهِ عَلَى أَثَرِ طَوَافٍ مُعْتَدٍ بِهِ وَكَذَا إِذَا أَعَادَ الطَّوَافَ وَلَمْ يُعِدِ السَّعْيَ فِي الصَّحِيحِ
ترجمہ اور جس شخص نے اپنے عمرہ کے واسطے بغیر وضو کے طواف وسعی کی اور حلال ہو گیا تو جب تک مکہ میں ہے ان دونوں کا اعادہ کرے اور اس پر کوئی چیز واجب نہیں ہے۔ بہر حال طواف کا اعادہ تو اس لئے کہ حدث کی وجہ سے اس میں نقصان پیدا ہو گیا ہے اور اگر طواف کا اعادہ کرنے سے پہلے وہ اپنے وطن واپس چلا گیا تو اس پر قربانی واجب ہے کیونکہ طواف کے اندر طہارت ترک ہو گئی ہے اور اس کو واپس آنے کا حکم نہ کیا جائے گا۔ کیونکہ رکن ادا کرنے سے حلال ہونا پایا گیا ہے۔ کیونکہ نقصان خفیف ہے اور اس پر سعی کے بارے میں کچھ واجب نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ وہ سعی کو ایسے طواف کے بعد لایا ہے جو شرعا معتبر ہے۔ اسی طرح اگر طواف کا اعادہ کیا اور سعی کا اعادہ نہیں کیا صحیح قول کے مطابق ۔
تشریح مسئلہ، اگر کسی نے اپنے عمرہ کے طواف اور سعی بین الصفا والمروہ کو بغیر وضو کیا اور حلال ہو گیا یعنی احرام سے نکل گیا تو جب تک شخص مکہ میں موجود ہے اس پر ان دونوں کا اعادہ واجب ہے اور دم وغیرہ کوئی چیز واجب نہیں ہے۔ طواف کا اعادہ تو اس لئے واجب ہے کہ حدث کی وجہ سے اس میں نقص پیدا ہو گیا ہے۔ پس اس نقص کو دور کرنے کے لئے طواف کا اعادہ کرے اور سعی اگر چہ طہارت کی محتاج نہیں ہے لیکن اس کے باوجود سعی کا اعادہ اس لئے واجب ہے کہ سعی طواف کے تابع ہے۔ پس جب طواف کا اعادہ کیا تو وہ بھی اس طواف کے بعد ہوگی۔ بہر حال جب اس نے دونوں کا اعادہ کر لیا تو اب اس پر بطور تاوان کوئی چیز واجب نہ ہوگی ۔ کیونکہ پیدا شدہ نقصان اعادہ سے دور ہو گیا ہے۔ اور اگر یہ شخص طواف کا اعادہ کرنے سے پہلے اپنے وطن واپس آ گیا تو اس پر دم واجب ہوگا۔ کیونکہ طواف کے اندر طہارت چھوڑ دی ہے حالانکہ طہارت واجب ہے۔ پس اس نقصان کی تلافی کرنے کے لئے دم واجب ہوگا۔ اور اس کو وطن سے واپس مکہ آنے کا حکم نہیں کیا جائے گا۔ کیونکہ طواف اور سعی جو عمرہ کے ارکان ہیں ان کو ادا کر کے حلال ہوا ہے۔ اور جو نقصان پیدا ہوا تھا وہ بہت معمولی ہے۔ اس لئے لوٹ کر مکہ آنے کی کوئی ضرورت نہیں ہے۔ اور اسپر سعی کے بارے میں کوئی چیز واجب نہ ہوگی ۔ کیونکہ اس نے بھی ایسے طواف کے بعد کی ہے جو شرعاً معتبر ہے۔ اسی طرح سعی کے بارے میں اس وقت کچھ واجب نہ ہوگا جبکہ اس نے طواف کا اعادہ کیا اور سعی کا اعادہ نہیں کیا ہے۔ یہی صحیح قول ہے اگر چہ بعض حضرات اس صورت میں دم واجب کرتے ہیں۔
And whoever performs tawaf for his Umrah and sa'y without wudu and becomes halal, then as long as he is in Makkah, he repeats both, and nothing is upon him. As for the repetition of tawaf, because the deficiency in it due to hadath is possible, and as for sa'y, because it is a follower of tawaf. And if he repeats both, nothing is upon him because the deficiency is removed. And if he returns to his family before he repeats, then upon him is a dam for leaving purification in it, and he is not ordered to return because the tahlul has occurred by performing the rukn, since the deficiency is minor. And there is nothing upon him in sa'y because he performed it following a tawaf that is considered valid. And likewise if he repeats the tawaf and does not repeat the sa'y in the correct [view].
Source pages p. 441

Commentary
This passage provides a ruling for Umrah. A person who performs tawaf and sa'y for Umrah without wudu and then becomes halal (cuts hair) must repeat both acts while still in Makkah, with no penalty. The repetition of tawaf is required because the deficiency caused by lack of wudu must be rectified. The sa'y must also be repeated because it follows the tawaf (it is a follower, taba'). If the person does not repeat and returns home, only a dam is due for the tawaf (because purification is wajib in tawaf), but no dam for sa'y because sa'y does not require purification and was performed after a tawaf that is considered valid (though deficient). There is no obligation to return to Makkah because the deficiency is minor and the rukn (tawaf and sa'y) has been performed, resulting in tahlul. The correct view is that if one repeats the tawaf but not the sa'y, no dam is due for sa'y, though some scholars hold otherwise.

Key Terms
سعى (sa'y): The walking between the hills of Safa and Marwah as a ritual of Hajj or Umrah.
تبع (taba'): Follower; sa'y is considered a follower of tawaf, so its ruling depends on tawaf.
تحلل (tahlul): The state of being released from ihram after performing the rituals.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person performs Umrah tawaf and sa'y without wudu and then returns home without repeating, what penalty is required according to the Hanafi school?
A) No penalty
B) A dam for tawaf only
C) A dam for both tawaf and sa'y
D) Return to Makkah to repeat

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, tawaf without wudu is valid but requires compensation (repetition or dam), while sa'y does not require wudu and incurs no penalty on its own.

Hajj — Pilgrimage
beginner

Ruling on Leaving Sa'y in Hajj
Ruling that leaving sa'y requires dam but Hajj is still valid

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on omitting sa'y in Hajj and explain why the Hajj remains valid despite the omission.

Core Idea
Omitting sa'y does not break Hajj — it only demands a dam.

This lesson presents a concise Hanafi ruling: Sa'y between Safa and Marwah is a wajib act in Hajj and Umrah. If a pilgrim omits it, the Hajj is still valid but a dam (sacrificial animal) is due. This distinction between wajib and rukn is central to the Hanafi school, setting it apart from other madhahib.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is sa'y (walking between Safa and Marwah). The ruling is that leaving sa'y requires a dam (penalty), but the Hajj remains valid.
2
Understand the legal category
The text states sa'y is from the wajibat (obligatory acts) in the Hanafi school. Note that wajib is distinct from fard (pillar). Omission of wajib requires compensation, not invalidation.
This is a key Hanafi principle: wajib omission → dam; rukn omission → invalid.
3
Note the cross-madhhab difference
The phrase 'according to us' (indana) signals that other schools disagree. For example, the Shafi'i school considers sa'y a rukn, so omission would invalidate Hajj.
Understanding these differences prevents confusion when studying fiqh comparitively.
4
Apply the ruling to a scenario
If a pilgrim forgets sa'y and returns home, they must offer a dam (sheep or equivalent) and their Hajj is accepted. No need to repeat Hajj.
The dam is offered in Makkah or can be compensated by fasting or charity if unable to slaughter? In Hanafi, dam is specific to sacrifice, not fasting.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
سعی کے ترک سے دم لازم ہے
وَمَن تَرَكَ السَّعَى بَيْنَ الصَّفَا وَالْمَرْوَةِ فَعَلَيْهِ دَمٌ وَحَجَّتُهُ تَامَّةٌ لِأَنَّ السَّعَى مِنَ الْوَاجِبَاتِ عِنْدَنَا فَيَلْزَمُ بِتَرْكِهِ
And whoever leaves the sa'y between Safa and Marwah, upon him is a dam, and his Hajj is complete, because sa'y is from the wajibat according to us, so it is binding by leaving it.
Source pages p. 441

Commentary
This is a concise ruling from the Hanafi school: Sa'y (walking between Safa and Marwah) is a wajib (obligatory) act in Hajj and Umrah. If a person omits it, a dam (sacrifice of a sheep or equivalent) is due as compensation, but the Hajj remains valid (Hajjatuhu tammah). This is because sa'y is not a rukn (pillar) in the Hanafi school; omitting a rukn invalidates the act, but omitting a wajib requires a penalty. The phrase 'according to us' (indana) indicates this is a distinct Hanafi position, in contrast to the Shafi'i school which considers sa'y a rukn.

Key Terms
سعى (sa'y): The ritual walking between Safa and Marwah.
دم (dam): A sacrificial animal (sheep or goat) offered as penalty for omission of a wajib in Hajj/Umrah.
واجب (wajib): An obligatory act that if omitted requires compensation but does not invalidate the ritual.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the consequence of completely omitting sa'y between Safa and Marwah in Hajj?
A) Hajj is invalid and must be repeated
B) A dam is required and Hajj is valid
C) Only a small charity is required
D) No penalty if omitted unintentionally

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, sa'y is wajib; its omission requires a dam but does not invalidate Hajj.

Ruling on Tawaf and Sa'y Without Wudu
Detailed ruling on Umrah tawaf and sa'y without wudu

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for tawaf and sa'y performed without wudu, distinguish between the scenarios of being in Makkah versus having returned home, and determine when a dam is required.

Core Idea
Tawaf without wudu is deficient but not invalid; repetition or a dam compensates the deficiency.

A common worship scenario during Umrah is completing tawaf and sa'y without wudu, whether due to forgetfulness or urgency. The Hanafi school provides a clear ruling that balances the validity of the acts with the requirement of purification. This lesson unpacks the passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah, explaining the two possible outcomes and the reasoning behind them, including the subordinate role of sa'y to tawaf.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and the Deficiency
Recognize that tawaf performed without wudu has a deficiency (naqs) due to the state of impurity. The passage states that this deficiency is not severe enough to invalidate the entire Umrah but requires remedy.
The deficiency is considered minor (yasir), hence the Umrah remains valid.
2
Distinguish the Two Scenarios
Trace the ruling based on the pilgrim's location: (a) if still in Makkah, both tawaf and sa'y must be repeated without any additional penalty; (b) if the pilgrim has already returned home, a dam (sacrificial animal) is required for tawaf, but no return to Makkah is necessary, and sa'y incurs no extra penalty.
The key factor is whether the deficiency can be removed by immediate repetition or must be compensated later.
3
Understand the Reasoning (Talil)
The passage explains that repeating tawaf removes the deficiency caused by impurity. Sa'y is repeated because it is subordinate to tawaf (taba'). If the pilgrim returns home, the deficiency in tawaf is compensated by a dam, and since the pillar (rukn) of tawaf has been performed, tahallul is valid.
The principle: a minor deficiency in a rukn does not invalidate the act but requires compensation.
4
Note the Intra-Madhhab Difference
Some Hanafi scholars hold that if tawaf is repeated but sa'y is not, a dam is still required for leaving sa'y. However, the sound opinion (sahih qawl) is that no dam is due because sa'y was performed after a valid tawaf.
The mufta bihi (operative ruling) is the sound opinion: no additional dam.

ترک ہو گئی ہے اور اس کو واپس آنے کا حکم نہ کیا جائے گا۔ کیونکہ رکن ادا کرنے سے حلال ہونا پایا گیا ہے۔ کیونکہ نقصان خفیف ہے اور اس پر سعی کے بارے میں کچھ واجب نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ وہ سعی کو ایسے طواف کے بعد پس اس نقص کو دور کرنے کے لئے طواف کا اعادہ کرے اور سعی اگر چہ طہارت کی محتاج نہیں ہے لیکن اس کے باوجود سعی کا اعادہ اس لئے واجب ہے کہ سعی طواف کے تابع ہے۔ پس جب طواف کا اعادہ کیا تو وہ بھی اس طواف کے اور سعی جو عمرہ کے ارکان ہیں ان کو ادا کر کے حلال ہوا ہے۔ اور جو نقصان پیدا ہوا تھا وہ بہت معمولی ہے۔ اس لئے لوٹ کر مکہ آنے کی کوئی ضرورت نہیں ہے۔ اور اسپر سعی کے بارے میں کوئی چیز واجب نہ ہوگی۔ کیونکہ اس نے بھی ایسے طواف کے بعد کی ہے جو شرعاً معتبر ہے۔ اسی طرح سعی کے بارے میں اس وقت کچھ واجب نہ ہوگا جبکہ اس نے طواف کا اعادہ کیا اور سعی کا اعادہ نہیں کیا ہے۔ یہی صحیح قول ہے اگر چہ بعض حضرات اس صورت میں دم واجب کرتے ہیں۔
And whoever performed tawaf for his 'Umrah and sa'y without wudu and became halal, then as long as he is in Makkah, he repeats both, and nothing is upon him. As for repeating tawaf, it is because the deficiency in it occurred due to the state of impurity. And as for sa'y, because it follows tawaf. And when he repeats both, nothing is upon him due to the removal of the deficiency. And if he returned to his family before repeating, then upon him is a dam for leaving purification in it, and he is not ordered to return because tahallul occurred by performing the pillar, since the deficiency is minor. And nothing is upon him regarding sa'y because he performed it following a tawaf that is valid according to sharia. Likewise, if he repeated tawaf and did not repeat sa'y, in the sound opinion. Translation: And the person who performed tawaf and sa'y for his 'Umrah without wudu and became halal, then as long as he is in Makkah, he should repeat both, and nothing is obligatory upon him. However, repeating tawaf is because a deficiency occurred in it due to impurity. And if he returned to his homeland before repeating tawaf, then a sacrifice is obligatory upon him because he left purification in tawaf. And he will not be ordered to return because tahallul occurred by performing the pillar, and the deficiency is minor. And nothing is obligatory upon him for sa'y because he performed it following a tawaf that is valid in sharia. Similarly, if he repeated tawaf and did not repeat sa'y, according to the sound opinion. Commentary: Issue: If someone performed the tawaf of 'Umrah and sa'y between Safa and Marwah without wudu and became halal, meaning he left ihram, then as long as the person is present in Makkah, repeating both is obligatory upon him, and nothing like a dam is obligatory. Repeating tawaf is obligatory because a deficiency occurred in it due to impurity. So to remove this deficiency, he should repeat tawaf. And sa'y, although it does not require purification, despite that, repeating sa'y is obligatory because sa'y is subordinate to tawaf. So when he repeated tawaf, it (sa'y) will also be after this tawaf. However, when he repeats both, then nothing is obligatory upon him as compensation because the deficiency that occurred is removed by repetition. And if this person returns to his homeland before repeating tawaf, then a dam is obligatory upon him because he left purification in tawaf, while purification is obligatory. So to compensate for this deficiency, a dam is obligatory. And he will not be ordered to return to Makkah from his homeland because he has become halal by performing the pillars of 'Umrah (tawaf and sa'y). And the deficiency that occurred is very minor. Therefore, there is no need to return to Makkah. And nothing will be obligatory upon him for sa'y because he performed it following a tawaf that is valid in sharia. Similarly, nothing will be obligatory for sa'y when he repeated tawaf and did not repeat sa'y. This is the sound opinion, although some scholars make a dam obligatory in this case.
Source pages p. 441

Commentary
This passage is a detailed ruling from the Hanafi fiqh commentary on the case of someone who performs the tawaf and sa'y for 'Umrah without wudu (ritual ablution) and then becomes halal (releases ihram). The passage is an expansion of the original matn, explaining the ruling and its rationale. The ruling distinguishes two scenarios: if the person is still in Makkah, he must repeat both tawaf and sa'y without any additional penalty; if he has already returned home before repeating, he owes a dam (sacrifice) for omitting wudu in tawaf, but is not required to return to Makkah because the deficiency is considered minor. The passage also explains that sa'y is subordinate to tawaf, so if tawaf is repeated, sa'y should also be repeated; if only tawaf is repeated and not sa'y, no penalty is due according to the sound opinion, though some scholars disagree. The reasoning is based on the idea that the deficiency (naqs) in tawaf caused by the lack of wudu is removed by repetition, and since the person has already validly performed the pillars (arkan) of 'Umrah, the remedy is minimal.

Key Terms
طواف (tawaf): Circumambulation of the Ka'bah; one of the pillars of 'Umrah and Hajj.
سعی (sa'y): Walking between the hills of Safa and Marwah; wajib in the Hanafi school for both Hajj and 'Umrah.
دم (dam): A sacrificial animal (sheep or goat) required as compensation for omitting a wajib or violating a prohibition in Hajj/'Umrah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) He must return to Makkah to repeat both.
B) He owes a dam but is not required to return.
C) Nothing is required because the Hajj is void.
D) He must repeat only sa'y.

Key Takeaway
Tawaf without wudu creates a deficiency that is remedied by repetition in Makkah or by a dam if the pilgrim has already returned home; the sa'y follows the tawaf and incurs no separate penalty.

Ruling on Omitting Sa'y: Dam Yes, Invalidation No
Ruling with reason on omission of sa'y

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on omitting sa'y and distinguish between wajib and rukn in Hajj.

Core Idea
Leaving sa'y requires a dam — it's wajib, not a rukn, so Hajj remains valid.

This passage is a ruling statement that clarifies the legal status of sa'y (the ritual walking between Safa and Marwah) in the Hanafi school. It directly addresses a common concern: whether omitting sa'y invalidates the entire Hajj. The author states the ruling concisely — a dam (sacrificial animal) is required, but the Hajj is valid — and provides the reason: in our school, sa'y is among the wajibat, not the arkan.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Pinpoint the act under discussion: sa'y between Safa and Marwah. Determine its hukm level: according to the Hanafi school, it is wajib (obligatory but not a rukn).
2
State the consequence of omission
If a pilgrim omits sa'y, the consequence is a dam (sacrifice), not the invalidation of the Hajj. The Hajj remains valid and complete.
3
Recognize the Hanafi position
Understand that this ruling is specific to the Hanafi school, based on their classification of sa'y as wajib. Other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) consider it a rukn, which would invalidate the Hajj if omitted.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَمَن تَرَكَ السَّعَى بَيْنَ الصَّفَا وَالْمَرْوَةِ فَعَلَيْهِ دَمْ وَ حَجَّتُهُ تَامُ لِأَنَّ السَّعَى مِنَ الْوَاجِبَاتِ عِندَنَا فَيلزم بتركه الدَّمُ دُونَ الْفَسَادِ. ترجمہ: اور جس نے (حج میں) سعی بین الصفا والمروہ چھوڑ دی تو اس پر دم واجب ہے اور اس کا حج پورا ہے۔ اس لئے کہ ہمارے نزدیک سعی واجبات میں سے ہے۔ لہذا اس کے ترک کرنے کی وجہ سے دم واجب ہوگا نہ کہ فساد حج۔ تشریح: واضح ہے۔
And whoever left the sa'y between Safa and Marwah, then upon him is a dam, and his Hajj is complete, because sa'y is among the wajibat in our school. So its omission necessitates the dam without invalidation. Translation: And whoever left (in Hajj) the sa'y between Safa and Marwah, then upon him is a dam, and his Hajj is perfect. Because in our school, sa'y is among the obligations. Therefore, its omission necessitates a dam, not the invalidation of Hajj. Commentary: It is clear.
Source pages p. 442

Commentary
This is a concise ruling from the Hanafi fiqh commentary. It states that if a person omits the sa'y (the ritual walking between Safa and Marwah) during Hajj, he must offer a dam (sacrifice) as compensation, but his Hajj is still valid and complete. The reason given is that in the Hanafi school, sa'y is classified as wajib (obligatory but not a rukn), so its omission does not invalidate the pilgrimage but requires a sacrificial penalty. This is in contrast to the Shafi'i school, where sa'y is considered a rukn (pillar), so omission would invalidate Hajj. The commentary adds that this ruling is clear and unanimously agreed upon within the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
سعی (sa'y): The ritual walking between Safa and Marwah; wajib in Hanafi school.
دم (dam): A sacrificial animal required for omitting a wajib act in Hajj/Umrah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Omitting sa'y requires a dam but does not invalidate Hajj because sa'y is wajib, not a rukn.

Departing Arafat Before Sunset: The Dam Requirement
Inter-madhhab dispute on whether leaving Arafat before sunset requires a dam

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on leaving Arafat early, explain the proof from the Prophet's command, and compare it with the Shafi'i position.

Core Idea
Leaving Arafat before sunset requires a dam because prolonging stay until sunset is wajib.

One of the key debates in Hajj jurisprudence is whether departing Arafat before sunset necessitates a sacrificial animal (dam). The Hanafi school, along with Malik and Ahmad, holds that a dam is obligatory. Imam al-Shafi'i is reported to have two positions: one requiring a dam and another absolving the pilgrim. This lesson unpacks the proofs on both sides, focusing on the Hanafi reliance on the Prophet's explicit command and the distinction between rukn and wajib.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the exact ruling given by the author: dam is wajib for leaving Arafat before sunset, even before the Imam departs.
The ruling applies to those who stood during the daytime.
2
Identify the opposing view and its proof
Note al-Shafi'i's position (in one narration) that nothing is required. Understand his basis: the rukn is only the standing itself; prolongation is not a rukn, so no penalty.
Al-Shafi'i also has a second position agreeing with the Hanafi view.
3
Follow the Hanafi proof (dalil)
Read the two hadiths cited: the Prophet's command 'Depart after sunset' and his contrast with the polytheists. Understand how these establish that remaining until sunset is wajib.
The command is interpreted as obligatory in Hanafi usul (al-amr yufidu al-wujub).
4
Analyze the Hanafi response to the opposing proof
The Hanafi school distinguishes between rukn (which invalidates Hajj if omitted) and wajib (which requires compensation). Prolongation is wajib, not a rukn, so leaving it requires dam but does not invalidate the Hajj.
This distinction is central to the Hanafi position.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: in the Hanafi school, the pilgrim must offer a dam; in the Shafi'i view (one position), no penalty. Also note the nuanced scenarios: standing at night and returning to Arafat after sunset.
If one returns before sunset, there is an intra-Hanafi difference; after sunset, dam is not dropped.

وَمَنْ أَفَاضَ قَبْلَ الإِمَامِ مِنْ عَرَفَات فَعَلَيْهِ دَمٌ وَقَالَ الشَّافِعُ لَا شَيْ عَلَيْهِ لأنَّ الرُّكُن أصل الوقوف فلا يلزمُهُ بِتَرْكِ الا طَالَةِ شَيْء وَلَنَا أَنَّ الإِسْتِدَامَةَ إِلى غُرُوبِ الشَّمْسِ وَاجِبٌ لِقَوْلِهِ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ فَادْ فَعُوا بَعْدَ غُرُوبِ الشَّمْسِ فَيَجِبُ بِتَرْكِهِ الدَّمُ بِخِلافِ مَا إِذَا وَقَفَ لَيْلا لأنَّ اسْتِدَامَةَ الْوُقُوفِ عَلَى مَنْ وَقَفَ نَهَا رَا لَا لَيْلًا فَإِنْ عَادَ إِلى عَرَفَةَ بَعْدَ غُرُوبِ الشَّمْسِ لَا يَسْقُطُ عَنْهُ الدَّمُ فِى ظَاهِرِ الرَوَايَةِ لأنَّ الْمَشْرُوكَ لَا يَصِيرُ مُسْتَدْرَكَا وَاخْتَلَفُوا فِيْمَا إِذَا عَادَ قَبْلَ الْغُرُوبِ. ترجمہ: اور جو شخص عرفات سے امام سے پہلے چل دیا تو اس پر دم واجب ہے اور امام شافعی نے فرمایا ہے کہ اس پر کوئی چیز واجب نہیں ہے کیونکہ رکن تو اصل وقوف عرفہ ہے پس طواف کو ترک کرنے سے کوئی چیز واجب نہ ہوگی۔ اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ غروب تک برابر وقوف رکھنا واجب ہے۔ کیونکہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا ہے کہ تم غروب آفتاب کے بعد روانہ ہو پس اس کے ترک کرنے سے دم واجب ہوگا۔ برخلاف اس کے جب کسی نے رات میں وقوف عرفہ کیا۔ کیونکہ وقوف کو برابر رکھنا اس پر واجب ہے جس نے دن میں وقوف کیا نہ کہ رات میں۔ پھر اگر غروب آفتاب کے بعد وہ عرفہ کو واپس آیا تو ظاہر الروایہ کے مطابق اس سے دم ساقط نہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ جوز ما نہ چھوٹ گیا ہے اس کی تلافی نہیں ہو سکتی ہے۔ اور اس صورت میں اختلاف ہے جب وہ غروب سے پہلے واپس آیا۔ تشریح: مسئلہ، اگر کوئی شخص میدان عرفات سے آفتاب غروب ہونے سے پہلے ہی امام کے روانہ ہونے سے پیشتر روانہ ہو گیا تو اس پر دم واجب ہے۔ یہی قول امام مالک اور امام احمد کا ہے اور امام شافعی کا بھی ایک قول یہی ہے۔ اور امام شافعی کا دوسرا قول یہ ہے کہ اس پر کوئی چیز واجب نہیں ہے۔ امام شافعی کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ رکن حج نفس وقوف عرفہ ہے جیسا کہ حدیث مَنْ وَقَفَ بِعَرُفَةً ثُمَّ حُجُہ سے پت چلتا ہے وقوف کو دراز کرنا حج کا رکن نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے وقوف عرفہ کو غروب تک دراز نہ کرنے کی وجہ سے دم وغیر و لا زم نہ ہو گا۔ ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ غروب آفتاب تک وقوف کو دراز اور ممتد کرنا واجب ہے۔ چنانچہ رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم کا ارشاد ہے فَادْفَعُوا بَعْدَ غُرُوبِ الشَّمْس - یعنی تم لوگ عرفات سے غروب آفتاب کے بعد روانہ ہوا کرو۔ اور ایک روایت میں ہے کہ آپ نے خطبہ میں فرمایا اما بعد فَإِنَّ أَهْلَ الشَّرُكِ كَانُوا يُدَافِعُوْنَ مِنْ هَذَا الْمَوْضِع إِذَا كَانَتِ الشَّمْسُ عَلَى رُؤْسَ الْجِبَالِ مِثْل عمائم الرجال في وُجُوهِهَا وإِنَّا نَدْفَعُ بَعْدَ أن تغيب - یعنی مشرکین اس جگہ سے یعنی عرفات سے اس وقت روانہ ہوتے تھے جب آفتاب پہاڑوں کی چوٹیوں پر اس طرح ہوتا جیسے مردوں کے چہروں پران کی پگڑیاں اور دیکھو ہم تو غروب کے بعد کوچ کریں گے۔ ان دونوں حدیثوں سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ غروب تک وقوف کو دراز کرنا واجب ہے۔ اور یہ شخص چونکہ غروب سے پہلے روانہ ہو گیا ہے اس لئے واجب کو ترک کرنے کی وجہ سے دم واجب ہوگا۔
And whoever hastened from Arafat before the Imam, then upon him is a dam. And al-Shafi'i said: Nothing is upon him, because the rukn is the original standing, so nothing is required of him for leaving its prolongation. And our proof is that staying until sunset is wajib, due to his statement (peace be upon him): 'Depart after sunset.' So by leaving it, dam becomes wajib. Contrary to the case when one stood at night, because staying is wajib on one who stood during the day, not at night. Then if he returned to Arafat after sunset, the dam is not dropped from him according to the apparent riwayah, because what has been missed cannot be recovered. And they differed in the case when he returned before sunset. Translation: And whoever departed from Arafat before the Imam, then upon him is a dam. Imam al-Shafi'i said: Nothing is upon him, because the rukn is the original standing in Arafah, so no penalty is due for leaving its prolongation. Our proof is that remaining until sunset is wajib, because the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Depart after sunset.' So by leaving it, dam is obligatory. Contrary to the case when one stood at night, because continuing standing is obligatory only on the one who stood during the day, not at night. Then if he returned to Arafat after sunset, according to zahir al-riwayah, the dam is not dropped, because what has been missed cannot be recovered. And they differed on the case when he returned before sunset. Commentary: Issue: If a person departs from Arafat before sunset, even before the Imam's departure, then a dam is obligatory upon him. This is the saying of Imam Malik and Imam Ahmad, and also one saying of Imam al-Shafi'i. Another saying of Imam al-Shafi'i is that nothing is obligatory upon him. The proof of Imam al-Shafi'i is that the rukn of Hajj is the standing in Arafat itself, as indicated by the hadith 'Whoever stood in Arafat, his Hajj is complete'; prolonging the standing is not a rukn. Therefore, no dam is necessary for not prolonging standing until sunset. Our proof is that prolonging and continuing standing until sunset is wajib. The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'Depart after sunset.' And in another narration, he said in his sermon: 'Indeed, the polytheists used to depart from this place (Arafat) when the sun was on the tops of the mountains like the turbans on men's faces, but we depart after it sets.' These two hadiths indicate that staying until sunset is wajib. And since this person departed before sunset, he has left a wajib, so a dam is obligatory.
Source pages p. 442

Commentary
This passage presents an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the ruling for someone who departs from Arafat before the Imam (i.e., before sunset) during Hajj. The Hanafi school, along with Malikis and Hanbalis, holds that a dam (sacrifice) is obligatory because prolonging the standing until sunset is wajib, based on the Prophet's explicit command 'Depart after sunset.' Imam al-Shafi'i has two positions: one requiring a dam, and another that nothing is required because the rukn is only the standing itself, not its duration. The Hanafi rebuttal relies on the hadith as proof that the continuation (istidamah) is wajib. The passage also discusses nuances: if one stood at night (i.e., missed the daytime standing), there is no obligation to stay until sunset; if one returns after sunset, the dam is not dropped according to Zahir al-Riwayah, and there is a difference of opinion if one returns before sunset. The commentary clarifies that the Hanafi position is supported by the practice of the Prophet and contrasts with the pagan practice of departing early.

Key Terms
وقوف عرفہ (wuquf Arafat): The standing in Arafat on the 9th of Dhul Hijjah; a rukn of Hajj.
دفع (daf'): Departure from Arafat after sunset.
دم (dam): Sacrificial animal required for omitting a wajib in Hajj.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi ruling for someone who departs from Arafat before sunset?
A) Hajj is invalid.
B) A dam is required.
C) Nothing is required.
D) Fasting is required.

Key Takeaway
Leaving Arafat before sunset without returning obligates a dam in the Hanafi school because remaining until sunset is wajib, as established by the Prophet's command.

Ruling on Leaving Sa'y: Dam Required, Hajj Valid
States ruling on leaving sa'y requires dam but hajj valid

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on leaving sa'y in Hajj and explain why dam is required while the Hajj remains valid.

Core Idea
Sa'y is wajib, not a rukn — omission requires dam, but Hajj is valid.

This lesson clarifies the legal status of sa'y (the walking between Safa and Marwa) in Hajj according to the Hanafi school. Many pilgrims and even students confuse it with a pillar (rukn), but the Hanafi position is clear: sa'y is a wajib, and leaving it demands a compensatory sacrifice (dam) while the Hajj itself remains valid. Understanding this distinction is essential for correct practice and for appreciating the Hanafi framework of obligations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Its Ruling
The passage deals specifically with sa'y — the walking between Safa and Marwah. Identify that the ruling is about leaving (omitting) this act during Hajj.
The act is sa'y, not tawaf.
2
Determine the Legal Status (Wajib vs Rukn)
The passage states that sa'y is among the wajibat (obligations), not the arkan (pillars). This is the core legal classification. Understand that in Hanafi fiqh, wajib is established by zanni dalil and its omission requires compensation but does not invalidate the act.
Other schools may classify differently.
3
Consequence of Omission
Because sa'y is wajib, omitting it does not nullify the Hajj; rather, it necessitates a dam (a sheep or equivalent sacrifice). The passage explicitly says 'his hajj is complete' (valid).
Dam is a specific type of compensation for Hajj violations.
4
Note the Cross-Madhhab Difference
The passage implicitly contrasts with the Shafi'i view, where sa'y is a rukn. Recognize that the practical consequence is major: in the Shafi'i school, omitting sa'y invalidates Hajj unless made up.
This difference arises from different usul principles regarding the proof of sa'y.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمہ اور جس نے ( حج میں ) سعی بین الصفا والمروہ چھوڑ دی تو اس پر دم واجب ہے اور اس کا حج پورا ہے۔ اس لئے کہ ہمارے نزدیک سعی واجبات میں سے ہے۔ لہذا اس کے ترک کرنے کی وجہ سے دم واجب ہوگا نہ کہ فساد حج ۔ تشریح واضح ہے۔
Translation: And whoever left the sa'y between Safa and Marwah in Hajj, then upon him is a dam (blood sacrifice) and his hajj is complete. Because in our view, sa'y is from the wajibat. Therefore, due to its omission, dam becomes obligatory, not nullification of hajj. Explanation: clear.
Source pages p. 442

Commentary
This is a ruling statement from the Hanafi madhhab. It clarifies that sa'y (the walking between Safa and Marwa) is a wajib (obligatory) act in hajj, not a rukn (pillar). Therefore, if someone omits it, their hajj remains valid but they must offer a dam (a sheep or equivalent sacrifice) as compensation. This is a key distinction from other schools that consider sa'y a rukn. The phrase 'hajj is complete' means it is valid and not nullified by the omission. The reason given is that sa'y is from the wajibat, meaning it is obligatory but not a pillar.

Key Terms
سعى (sa'y): The walking between the hills of Safa and Marwah during Hajj or Umrah.
دم (dam): A blood sacrifice, typically a sheep or goat, required as compensation for omission of a wajib in Hajj.
واجب (wajib): An obligatory act whose omission requires compensation (dam) but does not invalidate the act.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a pilgrim leaves the sa'y between Safa and Marwah, what is the ruling?
A) Hajj is invalid and must be repeated.
B) Hajj is valid but a dam (sacrifice) is required.
C) No penalty is required because sa'y is sunnah.
D) Only sadqah is required.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, leaving sa'y in Hajj necessitates a dam while the Hajj remains valid because sa'y is wajib, not a rukn.

Leaving Arafat Before Sunset: Hanafi vs Shafi'i
Dispute on whether leaving Arafat before Imam requires dam.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on leaving Arafat before sunset and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument using the hadith of departure after sunset as proof.

Core Idea
Prolonging standing at Arafat until sunset is wajib; leaving early requires dam.

This passage presents the inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafis and Shafi'is regarding a pilgrim who departs Arafat before the Imam (before sunset). The Hanafi school holds that dam is obligatory because prolonging wuquf until sunset is a wajib act, while Imam al-Shafi'i considers the mere standing as the rukn and sees no penalty. Understanding this dispute clarifies the Hanafi methodology of deriving rulings from a hadith command.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contested ruling
Determine exactly what is in dispute: the ruling on a pilgrim who leaves Arafat before sunset (before the Imam).
2
State the Hanafi position and its proof
The Hanafi school holds that a dam is wajib. Their proof is the hadith: 'Depart after sunset.'
In Hanafi usul, an imperative (amr) indicates wujub.
3
State the Shafi'i position and its proof
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that nothing is required because the rukn is simply standing at Arafat, not its prolongation.
Shafi'i: The command is guidance, not obligatory.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafis respond by distinguishing between day and night standing: prolongation is wajib only for those who stand during the day, based on the hadith.
5
Consider the exception of returning
If the pilgrim returns to Arafat after sunset, the dam remains (zahir al-riwayah). If returning before sunset, there is ikhtilaf among Hanafi imams.
Abu Hanifa and Sahibayn: dam waived; Imam Zufar: dam remains.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَمَنْ أَفَاضَ قَبْلَ الإِمَامِ مِنْ عَرَفَات فَعَلَيْهِ دَمٌ وَقَالَ الشَّافِعُ لَا شَيْ عَلَيْهِ لأنَّ الرُّكُن أصل الوقوف فلا يلزمُهُ بِتَرْكِ الا طَالَةِ شَيْء وَلَنَا أَنَّ الإِسْتِدَامَةَ إِلى غُرُوبِ الشَّمْسِ وَاجِبٌ لِقَوْلِهِ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ فَادْ فَعُوا بَعْدَ غُرُوبِ الشَّمْسِ فَيَجِبُ بِتَرْكِهِ الدَّمُ بِخِلافِ مَا إِذَا وَقَفَ لَيْلا لأنَّ اسْتِدَامَةَ الْوُقُوفِ عَلَى مَنْ وَقَفَ نَهَا رَا لَا لَيْلًا فَإِنْ عَادَ إِلى عَرَفَةَ بَعْدَ غُرُوبِ الشَّمْسِ لَا يَسْقُطُ عَنْهُ الدَّمُ فِى ظَاهِرِ الرَوَايَةِ لأنَّ الْمَشْرُوكَ لَا يَصِيرُ مُسْتَدْرَكَا وَاخْتَلَفُوا فِيْمَا إِذَا عَادَ قَبْلَ الْغُرُوبِ
And whoever departed from Arafat before the Imam, then upon him is a dam. And al-Shafi'i said: nothing is upon him because the rukn is the original standing, so nothing is required by leaving its prolongation. And our proof is that prolongation until sunset is wajib due to his statement (peace be upon him): 'Depart after sunset.' So by leaving it, dam becomes obligatory. Contrary to when he stood at night, because prolongation is required of one who stood during the day, not at night. And if he returned to Arafat after sunset, the dam does not fall from him in the apparent narration because what has passed cannot be recovered. And they differed about when he returned before sunset.
Source pages p. 442

Commentary
This is an inter-madhhab dispute about the ruling of a pilgrim who leaves Arafat before the Imam (i.e., before sunset). The Hanafi position is that such a person owes a dam (blood sacrifice). Imam al-Shafi'i holds that nothing is required. The Hanafi proof is a hadith commanding departure after sunset, indicating that staying until sunset is wajib. The Shafi'i argument is that the rukn (pillar) is simply standing at Arafat at any time, not prolonging it. The Hanafi response distinguishes between day and night standing: prolongation is only wajib for those who stand during the day. The text also discusses returning: if one returns after sunset, the dam is not waived in the apparent narration (zahir al-riwayah) because the missed time cannot be recovered. There is ikhtilaf (disagreement) among Hanafi imams if the return is before sunset: Imam Zufar holds the dam remains, while Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn hold it is waived.

Key Terms
استدامة (istidāmah): The continuous prolongation of standing (wuquf) at Arafat until sunset.
ظاهر الرواية (zāhir al-riwāyah): The well-known and authoritative transmission within the Hanafi school, attributed to Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani's six books.
مشروك (mashrook): That which has already passed and cannot be recovered (the missed time of standing).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on a pilgrim who departs from Arafat before sunset (before the Imam)?
A) Hajj is invalid and must be repeated.
B) Nothing is required because standing at Arafat is the only rukn.
C) A dam (blood sacrifice) is required.
D) Only fasting is required as compensation.

Key Takeaway
Leaving Arafat before sunset violates the wajib of istidamah and requires dam; returning before sunset may waive it per the preferred view of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Ruling on Leaving Wuquf at Muzdalifah
States ruling that leaving wuquf at Muzdalifah requires dam

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that leaving wuquf at Muzdalifah requires a dam and explain why it is wajib.

Core Idea
Leaving wuquf at Muzdalifah requires dam because it is a wajib, not a rukn.

This lesson explains a concise ruling from the Hidayah: the standing at Muzdalifah is a wajib act in Hajj. If omitted, the pilgrim must offer a dam (sacrifice) as compensation, without invalidating the Hajj. Understanding this distinction between rukn and wajib is crucial for correct Hajj practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its legal status
The passage states that wuquf at Muzdalifah is from the wajibat (obligatory acts) of Hajj.
2
State the consequence of omission
If a pilgrim leaves this wuquf, the text says 'upon him is a dam' – a sacrifice is required.
3
Recognize the rationale
The reason given is 'because it is from the wajibat.' This indicates that the ruling is based on the classification of the act as a wajib, not a rukn.
In Hanafi fiqh, wajib acts require compensation if omitted but do not invalidate the Hajj.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَمَنْ تَرَكَ الْوُقوفَ بِالْمُزْدَلِفَةِ فَعَلَيْهِ دَمْ لِأَنَّهُ مِنَ الْوَاجِبَاتِ
And whoever left the standing at Muzdalifah, then upon him is a dam because it is from the wajibat.
Source pages p. 443

Commentary
This is a concise ruling statement: wuquf at Muzdalifah (the standing on the night of the 10th of Dhul Hijjah) is a wajib act in Hajj. If a pilgrim omits it entirely, they must offer a dam (sacrifice) as compensation. The reason given is that it is one of the wajibat. Unlike the rukn (like standing at Arafat), the omission of a wajib does not nullify Hajj but requires a penalty.

Key Terms
الوقوف بالمزدلفة (al-wuquf bi al-Muzdalifah): The act of standing or staying at Muzdalifah on the night of the 10th of Dhul Hijjah after departing from Arafat.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) A dam (sacrifice) is required.
C) No penalty because it is sunnah.
D) Fasting is required.

Key Takeaway
Wuquf at Muzdalifah is wajib; leaving it requires a dam, but the Hajj remains valid.

Ruling on Leaving Rami al-Jimar All Days
States ruling on leaving rami all days requires one dam

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on omitting rami al-jimar entirely, explain why one dam suffices, and distinguish the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding the timing of the dam's obligation.

Core Idea
One dam for all missed rami because the acts are one kind; but the dispute is when dam becomes due—on delay or after the days?

This passage addresses a pilgrim who completely neglects the stoning of the jamarat over the four days of Hajj. The Hanafi school rules that one dam is sufficient for the entire omission, based on the principle that all rami acts are a single continuous obligation. The key dispute among Hanafi imams is whether merely delaying the rami within the days triggers the dam or only after the days have fully passed.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position on omitting all rami
Identify that the act (rami) is wajib and that completely omitting it requires one dam (sacrifice). Note that this is the agreed position of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn (the two disciples).
The dam is a penalty (jaza') for neglecting a wajib.
2
Explain the reasoning: unity of kind (jins mutahid)
The text states that one dam suffices because all rami acts are of one type (jins). This is analogous to shaving the head (halq), which also requires one dam if omitted. Understand that multiple acts of the same category are treated as a single obligation.
Analogy (qiyas) to halq: both are wajib acts of Hajj whose omission is compensated by one dam.
3
Identify the timing of the omission
The omission is only fully realized at sunset of the last day of rami (13th Dhul Hijjah). Until then, the pilgrim can still make up the missed throws in order. After that, the omission is complete and dam is certainly due.
This timing is agreed upon by the Sahibayn, but Abu Hanifa adds a nuance.
4
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute: delay vs. completion
Abu Hanifa holds that dam becomes obligatory simply by delaying rami within the days (i.e., not performing on time), while the Sahibayn hold that dam is only required after the days have ended. Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf): a pilgrim who delays rami on the first day would owe a dam immediately according to Abu Hanifa, but not according to the Sahibayn.
The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is Abu Hanifa's view, as per the author of al-Hidayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَمَنْ تَرَكَ رَمْيَ الْحِمَارِ فِي الْأَيَّامِ كُلَّهَا فَعَلَيْهِ دَمُ لِتَحَقُقُ تَرْكِ الْوَاجِبِ وَ يَكْفِيْهِ دَمُ وَاحِدُ لِأَنَّ الْجِنْسِ مُتَحِدُ كَمَا فِي الْحَلْقِ وَالتَّرَكَ إِنَّمَا يَتَحَقَّقُ بِغُرُوبِ الشَّمْسِ مِنْ آخِرِ أَيَّامِ الرَّمِي لِأَنَّهُ لَمْ يَعْرِفُ قُرُبَةً إِلَّا فِيهَا وَ مَادَامَتِ الْأَيَّامُ بَاقِيَةً فَإِلا عَادَةُ مُمْكِنَهُ فَيَرْ مِنْهَا عَلَى التَّالِيفِ ثُمَّ بِتَأْخِيرِهَا يَجِبُ الدَّمُ عِندَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ خِلَافًا لَّهُمَا
And whoever left the stoning of the pebbles (jimar) in all the days, then upon him is a dam, because the omission of wajib is established. And one dam suffices him because the kind (jins) is one, just as in shaving (halq). And the omission is only realized by sunset of the last day of rami, because it is not known as an act of worship except in those days. And as long as the days remain, repetition is possible, so he throws them in order. Then by delaying it, the dam becomes obligatory according to Abu Hanifa, contrary to them (the Sahibayn).

Commentary
This passage covers the ruling of a pilgrim who fails to perform the stoning of the jamarat (ramy al-jimar) on all four days (10th to 13th of Dhul Hijjah). The Hanafi school holds that rami is wajib. If someone omits all of it, one dam (sacrifice) is sufficient because the entire act is one continuous obligation, similar to shaving the head (halq) which requires one dam for omission. The omission is not considered complete until the sunset of the last day of rami (the 13th), because until then the pilgrim can still make up the missed throws. The text then mentions an intra-Hanafi dispute: according to Abu Hanifa, the simple delay (even within the days) makes the dam obligatory — meaning if one delays rami within the days without a valid excuse, dam is due. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) disagree; they likely hold that dam is only required after complete omission (i.e., after the last day). The relied-upon position is that of Abu Hanifa for immediate obligation upon delay.

Key Terms
رمي الجمار (ramy al-jimār): The act of throwing seven pebbles at each of the three jamarat (stone pillars) on specific days of Hajj.
الجنس متحد (al-jins mutahid): The kind or category is one; all rami acts are considered a single type of worship, so one dam suffices for omission of all.

Ruling on Leaving Wuquf at Muzdalifah
States ruling that missing Muzdalifah stay requires sacrifice

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for leaving the stay at Muzdalifah and explain why it is wajib in the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Missing the stay at Muzdalifah requires a dam (sacrifice) because it is a wajib act of Hajj.

This short passage from Al-Hidayah establishes a key principle: every wajib act of Hajj, if omitted, incurs a penalty of dam. While the stay at Arafah is a rukn (pillar) that invalidates Hajj if missed, the stay at Muzdalifah is a wajib, so its omission requires sacrifice but does not nullify the Hajj itself.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the specific act being ruled upon? What is the consequence according to the text?
The act is leaving the stay at Muzdalifah; the ruling is that a dam (sacrifice) is required.
2
Locate the legal basis
What reason does the author give for this ruling?
The reason is: 'because it is from the wajibat' (the obligatory acts of Hajj). This indicates the stay is classified as wajib in the Hanafi school.
3
Distinguish wajib from rukn
Why is the consequence a dam rather than invalidation of Hajj?
In Hanafi fiqh, missing a rukn (like Arafat) invalidates Hajj, while missing a wajib (like Muzdalifah) requires dam but the Hajj remains valid.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Do other schools agree with this classification?
Some schools may consider Muzdalifah stay as sunnah or mustahab; the Hanafi school insists on wajib status.

Omitting All Stoning Days and the Dispute on Delay
Ruling on omitting all stoning days and the dispute on delay

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for omitting all stoning days, explain why one dam suffices, and distinguish the positions of Abu Hanifa and Sahibayn regarding the delay of stoning.

Core Idea
Missing all stoning days requires one dam; delaying a wajib also incurs dam according to Abu Hanifa but not the Sahibayn.

Stoning the pillars during Hajj is a wajib act. If a pilgrim neglects all stonings across the four days, the Hanafi school holds that a single dam is due. But what if he performs them late? This lesson unpacks the ruling, its reasoning, and an important intra-Hanafi difference on whether delay itself triggers a penalty.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Confirm that stoning (ramy al-jimar) in the days of Tashriq is wajib. What happens if a pilgrim omits it on all days?
The text states one dam is required for total omission.
2
Understand the reasoning for one dam
The text says one dam suffices because the 'jins' (category) is one, analogized to shaving the head. Explore why multiple acts of stoning are treated as a single wajib category.
Analogy: like complete shaving requires one dam, even though multiple hairs are removed.
3
Determine when omission is confirmed
The timing of 'tark' (leaving) is only established at sunset of the last stoning day (13th Dhul Hijjah). Until then, repetition is possible.
Thus, if one stones on the 13th, omission is not yet confirmed.
4
Examine the intra-Hanafi dispute on delay
Imam Abu Hanifa holds that even delaying the stoning (if done late) requires a dam. The Sahibayn disagree—only complete omission incurs a dam.
This ikhtilaf is based on a principle: does delay of a wajib act necessitate compensation?
5
Apply the dispute to a scenario
Consider a pilgrim who delays all stoning to the last day but completes them before sunset. According to Abu Hanifa, he owes a dam for the delay; according to Sahibayn, he owes only one dam for the initial omission (if any) or none if he completes them in time.
This shows the practical thamarah al-khilaf.

Source Text

ترجمہ اور جس نے تمام ایام میں رمی جمار ترک کیا تو اس پر قربانی واجب ہے کیونکہ ترک واجب ثابت ہو گیا ہے اور اس کو ایک قربانی کافی ہے اس لئے کہ جنس ممتد ہے جیسے حلق میں ہے اور ترک، ایام رمی کے آخری دن کے غروب آفتاب سے متحقق ہوگا۔ کیونکہ رمی کا عبادت ہونا معلوم نہیں ہوا مگر انہیں ایام میں اور جب تک ایام موجود ہیں تو اعادہ ممکن ہے۔ پس ترتیب کے ساتھ رمی کرے پھر رمی کی تاخیر سے قربانی واجب ہوگی امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک ،صاحبین کا اختلاف ہے۔

And whoever leaves the stoning of the pillars in all the days, upon him is a sacrifice because leaving the wajib is established, and one sacrifice suffices him because the category is one, just like in shaving. And leaving is only established by sunset of the last day of the stoning days because it is not known to be an act of worship except in them, and as long as the days remain, repetition is possible, so he stones them in order. Then for delaying it, the sacrifice becomes obligatory according to Abu Hanifa, contrary to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad).
Source pages p. 443

Commentary
This passage covers two issues: (1) If a pilgrim omits all stoning on all four days (10th to 13th Dhul Hijjah), one dam is required, because stoning is wajib and all stonings are of one category, so they overlap. (2) If one delays the stoning until after the prescribed time (i.e., after sunset of the 13th), it becomes a deliberate omission. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, delaying a wajib act itself necessitates a dam, while the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that delay alone does not require a dam unless the act is completely omitted. The commentary clarifies that the time of stoning extends until sunset of the 13th, and if one does all the stonings in order on that day, it is valid but delayed. Abu Hanifa says that delay of a wajib requires dam; the Sahibayn disagree.

Key Terms
رمی جمار (ramy al-jimar): Stoning the three pillars (Jamrat al-Ula, al-Wusta, al-Aqaba) during Hajj.
دم (dam): A sacrificial animal required as expiation.
تاخیر (ta'khir): Delaying a rite beyond its optimal time.

Penalties for Incomplete Stoning (Rami) during Hajj
Details penalties for omitting stoning by day or partial omission

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the penalties for incomplete stoning and determine whether a dam (sacrifice) or sadaqah (charity) is required based on the quantity omitted.

Core Idea
Missing an entire day's stoning requires a sacrifice; missing a few pebbles requires only charity.

Stoning the jamarat is a wajib rite of Hajj. The penalty for omission is graduated: the more you miss, the heavier the expiation. This passage from Al-Hidayah explains exactly when a dam (sacrifice) is required versus when sadaqah (charity) suffices, based on the principle that each day's stoning is one complete rite (nusuk).

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Stoning each day (10th-13th Dhul Hijjah) is wajib. Missing any part triggers a penalty. The passage distinguishes between missing an entire day, missing one of the three jamarat, and missing a few pebbles.
The ruling is from Zahir al-Riwayah; other schools may differ.
2
Apply the 'complete rite' principle
Each day's stoning of all three jamarat is considered one nusuk (rite). Missing the entire day's stoning means omitting one complete nusuk, which requires a dam.
3
Distinguish partial omission scenarios
If a pilgrim stones only two of the three jamarat on a day, the missing part is less than half of that day's nusuk, so sadaqah (half sa' per missed pebble) is due. But if the missing part exceeds half (e.g., missing two jamarat), a dam becomes necessary.
The threshold is 'majority' of the day's stoning.
4
Handle Jamrat al-Aqaba on the Day of Sacrifice
On the 10th, only Jamrat al-Aqaba is stoned. Missing all or most of it requires a dam; missing a few pebbles requires sadaqah per pebble.
This is analogous to the general rule for a single day.
5
Calculate sadaqah for individual pebbles
For one, two, or three missed pebbles, give half a sa' of wheat per pebble. If the total sadaqah reaches the value of a dam, one may reduce arbitrarily because the obligation is only charity for a small omission.
The cap prevents sadaqah from exceeding dam value.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ایک دن کی رمی چھوڑنے سے بھی دم واجب ہے
وَإِن تَرَكَ رَمْيَ يَوْمٍ فَعَلَيْهِ دَمٌ لِأَنَّهُ نُسُكَ تَامٌ وَمَنْ تَرَكَ رَمَى إِحْدَى الْحِمَارِ التَّلْثِ فَعَلَيْهِ الصَّدَقَةُ لأَنَّ الْكُلَّ فِي هَذَا الْيَوْمِ نُسُ وَاحِدٌ فَكَانَ الْمَشْرُوكَ أقَلَّ إِلَّا أَن يَكُونَ الْمَتَرُوكَ أكْثَرَ مِنَ النِّصْفِ فَحِينَئِذٍ يَلْزَمُهُ الدَّمُ لِوُجُودِ تَرْكِ الْأَكْثَرِ وَإِنْ تَرَكَ رَمَى جَمْرَةِ الْعَقَبَةِ فِى يَوْمِ النَّحْرِ فَعَلَيْهِ دَمٌ لِأَنَّهُ تَرَكَ كُلَّ وَظِيفَةِ هَذَا الْيَوْمِ رَميًا وَكَذَا إِذَا تَرَكَ الْأَكْثَرَ مِنْهَا وَإِنْ تَرَكَ مِنْهَا حِصَاةً اَوْ حِصَاتَيْنِ اَوْ ثَلثًا تَصَدَّقَ لِكُلِّ حِصَاةٍ نِصْفَ صَاعِ إِلَّا أن يَبْلُغَ دَمًا فَيَنْقُصَ مَا شَاءَ لأنَّ الْمَتَرُوكَ هُوَ الْأَقَلُّ فَتَكْفِيهِ الصَّدَقَةُ
ترجمہ .... اور اگر محرم نے کسی ایک دن کی رمی ترک کی تو اس پر ایک دم واجب ہے کیونکہ یہ بھی پورا ایک نسک ہے۔ اور جس نے تین جمرات میں سے ایک دن کی رمی کو ترک کیا تو اس پر صدقہ واجب ہے۔ کیونکہ تینوں جمرات کی رمی اس دن میں ایک ہی نسک ہے۔ پس متروک نصف سے کم ہوا۔ لیکن متروک اگر نصف سے زائد ہو تو اس وقت اس پر دم لازم ہوگا کیونکہ اکثر کا ترک پایا گیا۔ اور اگر یوم نحر میں جمرہ عقبہ کی رمی ترک کر دی تو اس پر دم واجب ہے کیونکہ اس نے اس روز کاری کا پورا وظیفہ چھوڑ دیا۔ اور ایسے ہی جب اس نے رمی کا اکثر چھوڑ دیا اور اگر اسنے رمی جمار میں سے ایک کنکری یا دو کنکری یا تین کنکریاں مارنی چھوڑ دیں تو ہر کنکری کے واسطے نصف صاع گندم صدقہ کرے لیکن اگر یہ صدقہ مل کر ایک بکری کی قیمت کو پہنچ جائے تو جس قدر چاہے کم کر دے۔ کیونکہ متروک تو نصف سے کم ہے اس لئے اس کو صدقہ دینا کافی ہوگا۔
تشریح مسئلہ، اگر محرم نے ایک دن کی رمی چھوڑ دی تو اس پر ایک قربانی واجب ہے۔ کیونکہ یہ بھی پورا ایک نسک ہے اور پورے ایک نسک یا اس کے اکثر کو ترک کرنے سے دم واجب ہو جاتا ہے اس لئے یہاں بھی دم واجب ہوگا۔ اور تمام ایام کی رمی کے ترک سے ایک ہی قربانی اس لئے واجب ہوئی کہ ان کی جنس متحد ہے اور جنس متحد میں تداخل ہو جاتا ہے۔ اور اگر محرم نے کسی دن تین جمروں میں سے ایک جمرہ کی رمی کو ترک کر دیا اور باقی دو جمروں کی رمی کی تو اس پر صدقہ واجب ہے، یعنی ہر کنکری کے عوض نصف صاع گندم ادا کرے۔ کیونکہ مینوں جمروں کی رمی اس دن میں ایک ہی نسک شمار ہوتا ہے، اور ایک جمرہ کی رمی نصف سے کم ہے اور ایک نسک کے نصف سے کم کو
And if he leaves the stoning of a day, upon him is a sacrifice because it is a complete rite. And whoever leaves the stoning of one of the three pillars, upon him is sadaqah because all are one rite in that day, so the left part is less. Except if the left part is more than half, then at that time a sacrifice is necessary due to leaving the majority. And if he leaves the stoning of Jamrat al-Aqaba on the Day of Sacrifice, upon him is a sacrifice because he left the entire function of that day in stoning. Likewise if he leaves the majority of it. And if he leaves one pebble or two pebbles or three, he gives charity for each pebble half a sa' of grain, unless it reaches the value of a sacrifice, then he may reduce as he wishes because the left part is less, so charity suffices him.
Source pages p. 444

Commentary
This passage details the penalties for incomplete stoning. (1) If a pilgrim omits all stoning on one of the days (10th-13th), a full dam is required because each day's stoning is a complete rite. (2) If he omits one of the three pillars on a given day but stones the other two, then since all three form a single rite for that day, missing less than half requires sadaqah for each missed pebble (half a sa' per pebble). But if he misses more than half of the stonings of that day, a dam is required. (3) On the Day of Sacrifice (10th), only one pillar is stoned (Jamrat al-Aqaba), so missing all of it requires a dam; missing the majority also requires a dam; missing few pebbles requires sadaqah per pebble. (4) If the total sadaqah reaches the value of a dam, one may reduce it arbitrarily because the obligation is only to give charity for the small omission.

Key Terms
نسک (nusuk): A rite of Hajj; stoning each day is considered one complete rite.
صدقہ (sadaqah): Charity, specifically half a sa' of wheat per missed pebble as expiation.
دم (dam): A sacrificial animal.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a pilgrim misses 4 pebbles out of 7 on one day of Tashreeq, what is required?
A) Sadaqah of half sa' per pebble
B) One dam
C) Nothing
D) Repeat the stoning

Key Takeaway
The penalty for incomplete stoning is graduated: missing a complete day or majority of a day requires a dam; missing few pebbles requires sadaqah.
