Rulings on Leaving Ramy During Hajj: Dam vs. Sadaqah
Ruling with proof: compensation for omitting ramy

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on omitting ramy and apply the threshold of majority to determine whether dam or sadaqah is required.

Core Idea
Leaving the ramy of an entire day or its majority requires a dam; leaving a minority requires only sadaqah per stone.

In this passage, the Hanafi master illustrates a key principle of Hajj compensation: the distinction between dam and sadaqah turns on the quantity omitted. We will see how the complete act of ramy for a day is a single nusuk, and the rule 'majority takes the ruling of the whole' governs the transition from sadaqah to dam.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
State that ramy of a full day (any day of Tashreeq) is a complete nusuk; omitting it entirely requires a dam.
The text says: لِأَنَّهُ نُسُكٌ تَامٌ (because it is a complete nusuk).
2
Identify the dalil
The proof is the rational analogy (qiyas) that a complete act, when omitted, requires full compensation (dam).
No explicit textual proof is cited; the reasoning is talil.
3
Apply the rule to partial omission
If one leaves ramy of only one jamrah (less than half of the day's ramy), sadaqah is due per stone, because all three jamarat form a single nusuk.
Leaving one jamrah is 'less than half', so only sadaqah.
4
Apply the majority exception
If the omitted portion exceeds half (e.g., 11 out of 21 stones), the ruling shifts from sadaqah to dam due to the principle: 'majority has the same ruling as the whole.'
The text: إِلَّا أَن يَكُونَ الْمَتْرُوكُ أَكْثَرَ مِنَ النِّصْفِ فَحِينَئِذٍ يَلْزَمُهُ الدَّمُ
5
Special case: Yawm al-Nahr
On the Day of Nahr, the only ramy function is Jamrat al-Aqabah. Omitting it entirely or its majority requires a dam.
Leaving the 'entire function' of that day triggers dam.
6
Minor omissions
Leaving 1, 2, or 3 stones (fewer than half) requires sadaqah of half a sa' per stone. If the total reaches value of a dam, the pilgrim may reduce the amount.
Because the omitted is less than half, sadaqah suffices.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِن تَرَكَ رَمْيَ يَوْمٍ فَعَلَيْهِ دَمٌ لِأَنَّهُ نُسُكٌ تَامٌ وَمَنْ تَرَكَ رَمْيَ إِحْدَى الْجِمَارِ الثَّلَاثِ فَعَلَيْهِ الصَّدَقَةُ لِأَنَّ الْكُلَّ فِي هَذَا الْيَوْمِ نُسُكٌ وَاحِدٌ فَكَانَ الْمَتْرُوكُ أَقَلَّ إِلَّا أَن يَكُونَ الْمَتْرُوكُ أَكْثَرَ مِنَ النِّصْفِ فَحِينَئِذٍ يَلْزَمُهُ الدَّمُ لِوُجُودِ تَرْكِ الْأَكْثَرِ وَإِنْ تَرَكَ رَمْيَ جَمْرَةِ الْعَقَبَةِ فِي يَوْمِ النَّحْرِ فَعَلَيْهِ دَمٌ لِأَنَّهُ تَرَكَ كُلَّ وَظِيفَةِ هَذَا الْيَوْمِ رَمْيًا وَكَذَا إِذَا تَرَكَ الْأَكْثَرَ مِنْهَا وَإِنْ تَرَكَ مِنْهَا حِصَاةً أَوْ حِصَاتَيْنِ أَوْ ثَلَاثًا تَصَدَّقَ لِكُلِّ حِصَاةٍ نِصْفَ صَاعِ إِلَّا أَن يَبْلُغَ دَمًا فَيَنْقُصَ مَا شَاءَ لِأَنَّ الْمَتْرُوكَ هُوَ الْأَقَلُّ فَتَكْفِيهِ الصَّدَقَةُ
ترجمہ: اور اگر محرم نے کسی ایک دن کی رمی ترک کی تو اس پر ایک دم واجب ہے کیونکہ یہ بھی پورا ایک نسک ہے۔ اور جس نے تین جمرات میں سے ایک دن کی رمی کو ترک کیا تو اس پر صدقہ واجب ہے۔ کیونکہ تینوں جمرات کی رمی اس دن میں ایک ہی نسک ہے۔ پس متروک نصف سے کم ہوا۔ لیکن متروک اگر نصف سے زائد ہو تو اس وقت اس پر دم لازم ہوگا کیونکہ اکثر کا ترک پایا گیا۔ اور اگر یوم نحر میں جمرہ عقبہ کی رمی ترک کر دی تو اس پر دم واجب ہے کیونکہ اس نے اس روز کاری کا پورا وظیفہ چھوڑ دیا۔ اور ایسے ہی جب اس نے رمی کا اکثر چھوڑ دیا اور اگر اسنے رمی جمار میں سے ایک کنکری یا دو کنکری یا تین کنکریاں مارنی چھوڑ دیں تو ہر کنکری کے واسطے نصف صاع گندم صدقہ کرے لیکن اگر یہ صدقہ مل کر ایک بکری کی قیمت کو پہنچ جائے تو جس قدر چاہے کم کر دے۔ کیونکہ متروک تو نصف سے کم ہے اس لئے اس کو صدقہ دینا کافی ہوگا۔
تشریح مسئلہ، اگر محرم نے ایک دن کی رمی چھوڑ دی تو اس پر ایک قربانی واجب ہے۔ کیونکہ یہ بھی پورا ایک نسک ہے اور پورے ایک نسک یا اس کے اکثر کو ترک کرنے سے دم واجب ہو جاتا ہے اس لئے یہاں بھی دم واجب ہوگا۔ اور تمام ایام کی رمی کے ترک سے ایک ہی قربانی اس لئے واجب ہوئی کہ ان کی جنس متحد ہے اور جنس متحد میں تداخل ہو جاتا ہے۔ اور اگر محرم نے کسی دن تین جمروں میں سے ایک جمرہ کی رمی کو ترک کر دیا اور باقی دو جمروں کی رمی کی تو اس پر صدقہ واجب ہے، یعنی ہر کنکری کے عوض نصف صاع گندم ادا کرے۔ کیونکہ متینوں جمروں کی رمی اس دن میں ایک ہی نسک شمار ہوتا ہے، اور ایک جمرہ کی رمی نصف سے کم ہے اور ایک نسک کے نصف سے کم کو چھوڑنے کی وجہ سے صدقہ واجب ہوتا ہے۔ اس لئے ایک جمرہ کی رمی چھوڑنے سے صدقہ واجب ہوگا۔ ہاں اگر چھوٹی ہوئی رمی نصف سے زائد ہے مثلاً متینوں جمروں پر کل اکیس (۲۱) کنکریاں پھینکی جاتی ہیں، اب اگر اس نے دس کنکریوں سے رمی کی اور گیارہ کنکریوں کو ترک کر دیا تو اس پر دم لازم ہوگا۔ کیونکہ اس صورت میں اکثر کا ترک پایا گیا اور اکثر کے لئے وہی حکم ہوتا ہے جو کل کے لئے ہوتا ہے۔ اور کل کو ترک کرنے سے دم واجب ہوتا ہے۔ لہذا اکثر کنکریوں کی رمی ترک کرنے سے بھی دم واجب ہو جائے گا۔ اور اگر یوم نحر میں جمرہ عقبہ کی رمی چھوڑ دی اور تیرہویں ذی الحجہ کا آفتاب غروب ہو گیا تو اس پر واجب ہوگا، کیونکہ یوم نحر میں پورا وظیفہ فقط جمرہ عقبہ کی رمی کرنا ہے۔ تو گویا اس نے اس دن کے پورے نسک اور وظیفہ کو ترک کر دیا ہے اور پورے نسک کو ترک کرنا موجب دم ہے، اس لئے یہاں بھی دم واجب ہوگا نہ اسی طرح اگر یوم نحر میں جمرہ عقبہ کی رمی کا اکثر چھوڑ دیا مثلاً چار کنکری چھوڑی تو بھی دم واجب ہوگا، کیونکہ لِلأُكْرِ حُكُمُ الکل کا قاعدہ معروف ہے۔ اور اگر کسی محرم نے وجوب کے بعد کسی جمرہ کی رمی میں سے ایک یا دو یا تین کنکریاں مارنی چھوڑ دیں یعنی چار سے کم چھوڑ دیں تو ہر کنکری کے واسطے نصف صاع گندم صدقہ کرے، لیکن اگر یہ صدقہ مل کر ایک بکری کی قیمت کو پہنچ جائے تو جس قدر چاہے کم کر دے۔ کیونکہ متروک تو نصف سے کم ہے اور نصف سے کم میں دم واجب نہیں ہوتا بلکہ صدقہ واجب ہوتا ہے، اور صدقے کی قیمت چونکہ دم کے برابر ہے اس لئے اس میں سے کچھ کم کر دے تا کہ دم کے برابر واجب نہ ہو ۔
If he leaves the ramy of a day, then a dam is obligatory upon him because it is a complete nusuk. And whoever leaves the ramy of one of the three jamarat, then sadaqah is obligatory upon him because all of them in this day are one nusuk, so the omitted is less. Except if the omitted is more than half, then at that time the dam becomes necessary due to the existence of leaving the majority. And if he leaves the ramy of Jamrat al-Aqabah on the Day of Nahr, then a dam is obligatory upon him because he left the entire function of this day in ramy, and likewise if he leaves the majority of it. And if he leaves one pebble, or two pebbles, or three pebbles from it, he gives in charity for each pebble half a sa' (of wheat), unless it reaches (the value of) a dam, then he may reduce as he wishes, because the omitted is the lesser, so sadaqah suffices him.
Source pages p. 444

Commentary
This passage provides the Hanafi rulings on the consequences of omitting ramy (pelting of the jamarat) during Hajj. It opens with the general rule: leaving the ramy of an entire day (any of the days of Tashreeq) necessitates a dam (sacrifice of a sheep or goat), because the ramy of a whole day is considered a complete act of worship (nusuk tamm). The reasoning is that a complete nusuk, when omitted, requires a dam. Next, it addresses leaving ramy of just one of the three jamarat on a given day. Since all three jamarat together form a single nusuk for that day, leaving only one (which is less than half) only requires sadaqah (charity) – specifically half a sa' of wheat per stone not thrown. The text explicitly states that if the omitted amount exceeds half (e.g., 11 out of 21 stones), then it becomes the majority, and the ruling shifts to requiring a dam, based on the principle that 'the majority has the same ruling as the whole' (lil-ukthri hukmu al-kull). The third scenario: on the Day of Nahr (10th Dhul Hijjah), the only function is ramy of Jamrat al-Aqabah. Therefore, leaving it entirely (or its majority) necessitates a dam, as the entire function of that day is abandoned. Finally, leaving only one, two, or three stones (i.e., fewer than half) requires sadaqah per stone, but if the total sadaqah reaches the value of a dam, one may reduce the amount to avoid equaling the dam, since the omission is less than half and only deserves sadaqah. The commentary reinforces these points and explains the underlying principles: unity of category (ittiḥād al-jins) leads to the imposition of a single dam for multiple omissions of the same type, and the principle that the majority takes the ruling of the whole.

Key Terms
رمي (ramy): Pelting of the jamarat (stone pillars) with pebbles during the days of Tashreeq.
دم (dam): A sacrificial animal (sheep or goat) required as compensation for certain omissions or violations during Hajj or Umrah.
صدقة (sadaqah): Charity given as compensation; in this context, half a sa' (approximately 1.5 kg) of wheat per pebble not thrown.
جمرة (jamrah): One of the three stone pillars (Jamrat al-Ula, al-Wusta, al-Aqabah) that are pelted during Hajj.
نسك (nusuk): A ritual act of worship during Hajj or Umrah; here specifically referring to the ramy of a day or the combined ramy of all jamarat.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a pilgrim leaves ramy of one jamrah on a day of Tashreeq (assuming he pelted the other two completely), what is required?
A) One dam
B) Sadaqah of half a sa' per stone
C) Nothing
D) Two dams

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school distinguishes between major and minor omissions of ramy: a full day or its majority requires a dam; less than half requires only sadaqah per stone, with a provision to reduce if the sadaqah equals the value of a dam.

Delay of Halq and Tawaf al-Ziyarah: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Presents the ikhtilaf between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on delay of halq and tawaf.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on whether delaying halq or tawaf al-ziyarah requires a dam, and explain the difference in their proofs.

Core Idea
A delayed Hajj ritual requires a dam according to Abu Hanifa; the Sahibayn say qada suffices.

The timing of Hajj rituals is governed by specific windows. When a pilgrim delays acts like halq (shaving) or tawaf al-ziyarah beyond their prescribed days, a difference arises among the Hanafi imams. Abu Hanifa relies on a hadith and analogical reasoning to require a dam, while the Sahibayn argue that making up the missed act (qada) is sufficient. This lesson dissects their proofs and the practical consequence of their ikhtilaf.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Acts in Dispute
Recognize that the passage discusses delaying halq, tawaf al-ziyarah, and ramy beyond their times, as well as giving precedence to one nusuk over another (e.g., halq before ramy).
2
State Imam Abu Hanifa's Position and Dalil
Imam Abu Hanifa requires a dam for such delay or precedence. His proof is the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud: 'Whoever gives precedence to one nusuk over another must offer a dam.' He also uses qiyas: just as leaving the miqat without ihram requires a dam, delaying a time-bound nusuk requires a dam.
3
State the Sahibayn's Position and Dalil
The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) hold that no additional penalty is needed; qada (make-up) of the missed act suffices. They argue that the purpose of compensation is fulfilled by performing the act later.
4
Compare and Contrast the Proofs
The Sahibayn's argument is rational (istiqra'), while Abu Hanifa relies on a specific textual proof (hadith) and analogy. Weigh the strength: the hadith is explicit, but its authenticity is not fully established; however, it is accepted in Hanafi fiqh.
5
Determine the Thamarah al-Khilaf
The practical difference: a pilgrim who delays halq until after 13th Dhul Hijjah must offer a dam according to Abu Hanifa, but no dam according to the Sahibayn. In fatwa, the relied-upon view is Abu Hanifa's.
The commentary suggests Abu Hanifa's view is stronger and is the mufta bihi.

وَمَنْ أَخَّرَ الْحَلْقَ حَتَّى مَضَتْ أَيَّامُ النَّحْرِ فَعَلَيْهِ دَمٌ عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ وَكَذَا إِذَا أَخَّرَ طَوَافَ الزِّيَارَةِ وَقَالَا لَا شَيْءَ عَلَيْهِ فِي الْوَجْهَيْنِ وَكَذَا الْخِلَافُ فِي تَأْخِيرِ الرَّمْيِ وَفِي تَقْدِيمِ نُسُكٍ عَلَى نُسُكٍ كَالْحَلْقِ قَبْلَ الرَّمْيِ وَنَحْرِ الْقَارِنِ قَبْلَ الرَّمْيِ وَالْحَلْقِ قَبْلَ الذَّبْحِ لَهُمَا أَنَّ مَا فَاتَ مُسْتَدْرَكٌ بِالْقَضَاءِ وَلَا يَجِبُ مَعَ الْقَضَاءِ شَيْءٌ آخَرُ وَلَهُ حَدِيثُ ابْنِ مَسْعُودٍ أَنَّهُ قَالَ مَنْ قَدَّمَ نُسُكًا عَلَى نُسُكٍ فَعَلَيْهِ دَمٌ وَلِأَنَّ التَّأْخِيرَ عَنِ الْمَكَانِ يُوجِبُ الدَّمَ فِيمَا هُوَ مُوَقَّتٌ بِالْمَكَانِ كَالْإِحْرَامِ فَكَذَا التَّأْخِيرُ عَنِ الزَّمَانِ فِيمَا هُوَ مُوَقَّتٌ بِالزَّمَانِ
ترجمہ: اور جس نے حلق کو مؤخر کیا یہاں تک کہ ایام قربانی گذر گئے تو اس پر ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک ایک دم واجب ہے اور ایسے ہی جب اس نے طواف زیارت کو مؤخر کیا اور صاحبین نے فرمایا کہ دونوں صورتوں میں اس پر کچھ واجب نہیں ہے۔ اور یہ اختلاف رمی کو مؤخر کرنے اور ایک نسک کو دوسرے نسک پر مقدم کرنے میں ہے۔ جیسے رمی سے پہلے حلق اور قارن کا رمی سے پہلے ذبح کرنا اور ذبح سے پہلے حلق کرانا۔ صاحبین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ جو چیز فوت ہوئی قضاء سے اس کی تلافی کر لی گئی ہے اور قضاء کے ساتھ کوئی دوسری چیز واجب نہیں ہوتی ہے۔ اور امام ابوحنیفہ کی دلیل حدیث ابن مسعود ہے فرمایا کہ جس نے ایک نسک کو دوسرے نسک پر مقدم کیا اس پر دم واجب ہے۔ اور اس لئے کہ جو چیز مکان کے ساتھ موقت کی گئی ہے جیسے احرام تو اس کو اس کے مکان سے مؤخر کر نا دم واجب کرتا ہے۔ پس اسی طرح جو چیز زمانہ کے ساتھ موقت کی گئی ہو اس کو زمانہ سے مؤخر کرنا موجب دم ہے۔
And whoever delays the shaving until the days of Nahr have passed, then a dam is obligatory upon him according to Abu Hanifah, and likewise if he delays the Tawaf al-Ziyarah; and the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: nothing is obligatory upon him in either case. And similarly the difference of opinion applies to delaying the ramy and to giving precedence of one nusuk over another, such as shaving before ramy, the Qarin sacrificing before ramy, and shaving before slaughtering. Their (Sahibayn's) proof: that what is missed is made up by qada, and with qada nothing else becomes obligatory. And his (Abu Hanifah's) proof: the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud that he said: 'Whoever gives precedence to one nusuk over another, then a dam is obligatory upon him'; and because delay from the place (intended) necessitates a dam in that which is time-bound by place, like ihram; thus also delay from the time (intended) in that which is time-bound by time.
Source pages p. 445

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the delay of certain Hajj rituals beyond their prescribed times or precedence of one over another. The core issue: Imam Abu Hanifa holds that delaying halq (shaving/trimming the head) until after the days of Nahr (10th-12th Dhul Hijjah) requires a dam, as does delaying Tawaf al-Ziyarah (the obligatory circumambulation). The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) disagree, holding that no compensation is needed if these acts are merely delayed, because the missed act can be performed as qada (make-up) and no additional penalty attaches. The same difference extends to delaying ramy (pelting) beyond its time, and to giving precedence to one nusuk over another (e.g., shaving before ramy, a Qarin sacrificing before ramy, or shaving before slaughtering). The Sahibayn's argument: qada suffices; no extra compensation is required. Imam Abu Hanifah's proof: the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud (marfu') stating that whoever gives precedence to one nusuk over another must offer a dam. Additionally, he draws an analogy (qiyas) with ihram: just as leaving the miqat (the appointed place for ihram) without entering ihram requires a dam because it is time-bound by place, similarly delaying an act that is time-bound (like halq having a specific time window) requires a dam. The commentary explains that this dispute is founded on the principle that Imam Abu Hanifah considers delay of a time-bound nusuk as compensable with a dam, while the Sahibayn consider qada sufficient without extra penalty.

Key Terms
حلق (halq): Shaving or trimming the head hair as an obligatory act of Hajj (wajib) performed after ramy on the Day of Nahr or within the days of Tashreeq.
طواف الزيارة (tawaf al-ziyarah): The obligatory circumambulation of the Ka'bah (also called tawaf al-ifadah) performed after returning from Mina on the 10th Dhul Hijjah or within the days of Nahr.
قضاء (qada): Making up a missed wajib act after its prescribed time.
تأخير (ta'khir): Delay of a ritual act beyond its prescribed time.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, what is required if a pilgrim delays halq (shaving) until after the days of Nahr have passed?
A) Nothing, as long as he eventually performs halq
B) A dam (sacrificial animal)
C) Sadaqah of half a sa' per day delayed
D) Expiation by fasting three days

Key Takeaway
Delaying a time-bound Hajj nusuk requires a dam per Imam Abu Hanifa (mufta bihi), while the Sahibayn hold that qada alone suffices.

Delaying or Advancing Hajj Rituals: Dam Obligation
Explaining the ruling on delaying or advancing Hajj rituals and the ikhtilaf between Abu Hanifa and Sahibayn.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on the obligation of dam for delaying or advancing Hajj rituals and evaluate the proofs for each view.

Core Idea
A delay in Hajj rituals may require a sacrifice according to Abu Hanifa, but the Sahibayn say qada' suffices.

In this passage, we explore an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the necessity of dam when a pilgrim delays a Hajj ritual beyond its prescribed time or performs one before another. Imam Abu Hanifa holds that such actions require a sacrificial animal, while the Sahibayn disagree, arguing that the missed ritual can simply be made up (qada'). This lesson will walk through the specific scenarios, the proofs from hadith and qiyas, and the practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue and each position
The issue is whether delaying or advancing a Hajj ritual (halq, tawaf al-ziyarah, ramy, etc.) requires a dam. State Abu Hanifa's view (dam wajib) and the Sahibayn's view (no dam, qada' suffices).
2
Analyze Abu Hanifa's proof
Abu Hanifa relies on the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud (or Ibn Abbas) that 'whoever advances one ritual over another, upon him is a dam.' He also uses qiyas with ihram: just as delaying ihram past the miqat incurs dam, delaying a time-bound ritual incurs dam.
The hadith directly addresses taqdim (advancing), and qiyas extends to takhir (delaying).
3
Analyze the Sahibayn's proof
The Sahibayn argue that what is missed is compensated by qada', and nothing else is obligatory with qada'. They compare it to missed prayer, where only qada' is required, no additional penalty.
Their qiyas focuses on the principle of compensation rather than penalty.
4
Note the thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference)
For example, if a pilgrim delays halq until after ayam al-nahr, Abu Hanifa says he must sacrifice a goat; the Sahibayn say he simply shaves later with no sacrifice.
This difference directly affects the pilgrim's financial and religious obligations.
5
Evaluate the mufta bihi
Later Hanafi authorities (e.g., al-Hidayah) adopt Abu Hanifa's view as the operative ruling. The hadith evidence is considered stronger, and the qiyas with ihram is preferred over the Sahibayn's analogy with prayer.
Although both views are legitimate, the mufta bihi is Abu Hanifa's.

جیسے حاجی اگر بغیر احرام کے میقات سے گذر گیا اور پھر احرام باندھا تو اس پر دم واجب ہو گا۔ اسی طرح جو نسک کسی زمانہ کے ساتھ خاص وہ اس کو اگر اس زمانہ سے مؤخر کر دیا جائے تو اس پر بھی دم واجب ہوگا ۔ ان دونوں کے درمیان جامع تاخیر کے نقصان کا پیدا ہوتا ہے۔
And whoever delays the shaving until the days of sacrifice have passed, upon him is a dam according to Abu Hanifa, and likewise if he delays the tawaf al-ziyarah. And they (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: nothing is upon him in both cases. And similarly the disagreement regarding delaying the stoning and regarding advancing one ritual over another, like shaving before stoning, and the qarin's sacrifice before stoning, and shaving before slaughter. Their proof is that what is missed is compensated by making it up (qada'), and nothing else is obligatory with qada'. And his proof is the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud that he said: Whoever advances a nusuk before another nusuk, upon him is a dam. And because delaying from the place necessitates dam in what is time-bound by place, like ihram; so similarly delaying from the time in what is time-bound by time.
Source pages p. 445

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and the two Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) regarding the obligation of dam when a pilgrim delays a ritual (such as halq, tawaf al-ziyarah, or ramy) beyond its prescribed time, or advances one ritual over another (e.g., halq before ramy, or sacrifice before ramy for a qarin). Abu Hanifa holds that such delay or advancement necessitates a dam, based on the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud (or Ibn Abbas) and an analogy with ihram: just as delaying ihram past the miqat incurs dam, delaying a time-bound ritual also incurs dam. The Sahibayn argue that the missed ritual can be performed as qada' (make-up) without additional penalty, similar to missed prayers. The dispute is practical: if a pilgrim delays halq until after the days of Nahr, Abu Hanifa says he must sacrifice a goat; the Sahibayn say no sacrifice is required, as the qada' suffices. The text elaborates various scenarios where this ikhtilaf applies: delaying ramy from its day, or performing halq before ramy, etc.

Key Terms
دم (dam): A sacrificial animal (a goat, sheep, or share in a cow/camel) offered as a penalty for violating a Hajj obligation.
نسك (nusuk): A ritual act of Hajj or Umrah, such as tawaf, sa'y, wuqoof, ramy, halq, etc.
تأخير (takhir): Delaying a ritual beyond its prescribed time or order.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the basis for Imam Abu Hanifa's ruling that delaying halq until after the days of Nahr requires a dam?
A) A hadith of Ibn Mas'ud that whoever advances one ritual over another owes a dam
B) Qiyas with delaying prayer
C) Ijma' of the Companions
D) The principle that any violation of time incurs a penalty

Key Takeaway
The obligation of dam for delayed or advanced Hajj rituals is contested within the Hanafi school, with Abu Hanifa's view supported by hadith and qiyas, while the Sahibayn rely solely on the principle of qada'.

Shaving Outside the Haram: Intra-Hanafi Ikhtilaf on the Penalty (Dam)
Intra-Hanafi dispute on tawqeet of halq for dam

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four Hanafi positions on whether shaving outside the Haram during Hajj/Umrah incurs a dam and apply the thamarah (practical consequence) to a given scenario.

Core Idea
Shaving outside the Haram incurs a dam according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, but not according to Abu Yusuf — the ikhtilaf is about tawqeet (binding by time/place).

This passage from al-Hidayah presents a classic intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on whether shaving (halq) as a concluding rite of Hajj or Umrah is restricted to the Haram and specific days. The ruling affects whether a pilgrim who shaves outside the sacred precinct must offer a dam (penalty sacrifice). Four positions emerge from the three eponymous imams and Imam Zufar. Understanding this dispute refines your ability to apply Hanafi tarjih in Hajj rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the disputed ruling
The act is shaving (halq) or shortening (qasr) the hair during Hajj or Umrah when done outside the Haram. The dispute is whether this incurs a dam (penalty).
The passage also mentions Umrah separately; the same principle applies.
2
List the four Hanafi positions
Abu Hanifa: halq is bound by both time (days of Nahr) and place (Haram) → violation of either requires dam. Muhammad: bound by place only → outside Haram = dam regardless of time. Zufar: bound by time only → outside prescribed days = dam regardless of place. Abu Yusuf: not bound by either → no dam for any violation of time or place.
These positions are recorded in al-Jami' al-Saghir and other sources.
3
Trace the dalil for each position
Abu Yusuf cites the incident of Hudaybiyyah where the Prophet (ﷺ) and Companions shaved outside the Haram (due to ihsar). Abu Hanifa and Muhammad argue that halq, as a nusuk, is analogous to sacrifice (dhabh) which is specific to the Haram; also, the sunnah of shaving at Mina (within Haram) supports place-restriction. They respond that Hudaybiyyah's location may have been within the Haram boundary, or the case was exceptional due to being prevented (ihsar).
Zufar's position is derived from a different interpretive framework.
4
Understand the response and tarjih
The author of al-Hidayah notes that the 'more correct' (asahh) is that there is ikhtilaf. The majority position (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) is usually followed in fatwa, requiring dam for shaving outside the Haram.
The mufta bihi is to be cautious and follow the majority.
5
Apply the thamarah al-khilaf
In practice, a pilgrim who shaves at a hotel in Jeddah (outside Haram) on the 12th of Dhul Hijjah: according to Abu Hanifa, dam wajib; according to Abu Yusuf, no dam. The mufta bihi is to offer dam.
All imams agree that halq itself is valid for tahlil (exit from ihram) regardless of place/time.

فَإِنْ حَلَقَ فِي أَيَّامِ النَّحْرِ فِى غَيْرِ الْحَرَمِ فَعَلَيْهِ دَمُ وَمَنِ اعْتَمَرَ فَخَرَجَ مِنَ الْحَرَمِ وَ قَصَرَ فَعَلَيْهِ دَمُ عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ وَ مُحَمَّدٍ وَ قَالَ أَبُو يُوسُفَ لَا شَى عَلَيْهِ قَالَ ذَكَرَ فِى الْجَامِعِ الصَّغِيرِ قولُ أَبِى يُوسُفَ فِى الْمُعْتَمِر وَلَمْ يَذْكُرْ فِى الحاج وَقِيلَ هُوَ بِالْإِنْفَاقِ لأنَّ السُّنَّةَ جَرَتْ فِي الْحَجِ بِالْخَلْقِ بِمِنى وَهُوَ مِنَ الْحَرَمِ وَالْأَصَحُ أَنَّهُ عَلَى الْخِلَافِ هُوَ يَقُولُ اَلْحَلْقَ غَيْرُ مُختَصّ بِالْحَرَم لأنَّ النَّبِيَّ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ وَأَصْحَابَهُ أحْصِرُ وَ بِالْحُدَيْبِيَّةِ وَحَلَقُوا فِي غَيْرِ الْحَرَمِ وَلَهُمَا اَنَّ الْحَلْقَ لَمَا جُعِلَ مُحَلّلاً صَارَ كَالسَّلَام فِي آخِرِ الصَّلوة فَإِنَّهُ مِنْ وَاجِبَاتِهَا وَإِنْ كَانَ مُحَلَّلًا فَإِذَا صَارَ نُسُكَا اِخْتَصَّ بِالحَرَمِ كَالذَّبْحِ وَبَعْضُ الْحُدَنِيَّةِ مِنَ الْحَرَمِ فَلَعَلَّهُمْ خَلَقُوا فِيهِ فَالْحَاصِلُ أَنَّ الْحَلْقَ يَتَوَفَّتُ بِالزَّمَانِ وَالْمَكَانَ عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةً وَعِندَ أبى يُوسُفَ لَا يَتَوَفَّتُ بِهِمَا وَعِنْدَ مُحَمَّدٍ يَتَوَفَّتُ بِالْمَكَانِ دُونَ الزَّمَانِ وَعِندَ زُفَرَ يَتَوَفَّتْ بِالزَّمَانِ دُونَ الْمَكَانِ وَهَذَا الْخِلَافُ فِى التوقِيْتِ فِى حَقِّ التَّضْمِيْنِ بِالدَّمِ أَمَا لَا يَتَوقَّتُ في حق التحلل بالاتفاق

ترجمہ پس اگر ایام نحر میں حرم کے علاوہ میں حلق کیا تو اس پر دم واجب ہے اور جس نے عمرہ کیا پھر حرم سے نکل گیا اور قصر کیا تو اس پر بھی دم واجب ہے امام ابو حنیفہ اور محمد کے نزدیک اور ابو یوسف نے فرمایا اس پر کچھ واجب نہیں ہے۔
For if he shaves during the days of sacrifice outside the Haram, upon him is a dam. And whoever performs Umrah and leaves the Haram and cuts (hair) short, upon him is a dam according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, and Abu Yusuf said: nothing is upon him. He said: it is mentioned in al-Jami' al-Saghir the statement of Abu Yusuf regarding the one performing Umrah, and he did not mention regarding the Hajj. And it was said he is in agreement because the sunnah in Hajj is shaving at Mina, which is part of the Haram. And the more correct is that there is disagreement. He (Abu Yusuf) says: shaving is not specific to the Haram because the Prophet (peace be upon him) and his Companions were prevented (from entering Mecca) at al-Hudaybiyyah and they shaved outside the Haram. And for them (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad): shaving, since it was made a cause of tahlil (exit from ihram), became like the salam at the end of prayer, for it is from its wajibat, and although it causes tahlil, when it becomes a nusuk, it is specific to the Haram like sacrifice. And part of al-Hudaybiyyah is from the Haram, perhaps they shaved within it. The conclusion is that shaving is time-bound and place-bound according to Abu Hanifa. And according to Abu Yusuf, it is not bound by either. And according to Muhammad, it is bound by place but not time. And according to Zufar, it is bound by time but not place. And this dispute is about time-binding in regard to the penalty of dam; as for binding in regard to tahlil (exit from ihram), there is agreement that it is not required to be within Haram or a specific time.
Source pages p. 446

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling on shaving (halq) or cutting hair (qasr) outside the Haram during the days of Nahr (10-13 Dhul Hijjah) for a Hajj pilgrim, and similarly for a person performing Umrah who leaves the Haram and cuts his hair. Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad hold that if one shaves outside the Haram during these days, a dam is required. Abu Yusuf disagrees and says no dam. The reason for the difference: Abu Hanifa considers halq to be ordained by both time (the days of Nahr) and place (the Haram), so violating either imposes a dam. Muhammad considers it ordained by place only (so outside the Haram incurs dam, but timing is flexible). Abu Yusuf considers it ordained by neither, so no dam for place or time violation. Zufar's view is that it is ordained by time only (so doing it outside the prescribed time incurs dam, but place is not restricted). The text clarifies that this ikhtilaf is regarding the penalty (dam) for violation; all agree that halq is necessary for tahlil (exit from ihram) regardless of place or time. The practical effect: a pilgrim who shaves in a hotel outside the Haram on the 12th of Dhul Hijjah would owe a dam according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, but not according to Abu Yusuf.

Key Terms
حلق (halq): Shaving the head, one of the concluding rites of Hajj/Umrah that causes tahlil (exit from ihram).
حرم (haram): The sacred precinct around Mecca and Mina, where certain rituals must be performed.
موقت (muwaqqat): Bound by a specific time or place; here referring to whether halq is restricted to the Haram and/or specific days.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following correctly describes the position of Imam Zufar on shaving (halq) for the purpose of dam?
A) Halq is bound by both time and place; violation of either requires dam.
B) Halq is bound by place only; violation of place requires dam.
C) Halq is bound by time only; violation of time requires dam.
D) Halq is not bound by either; no dam required.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school contains a legitimate four-way ikhtilaf on whether shaving outside the Haram incurs a dam; the mufta bihi follows the majority (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) requiring dam.

Hajj — Pilgrimage

Delaying Hajj Rituals and Obligation of Dam
Explains ruling on delaying Hajj rituals with intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on whether delaying or advancing Hajj rituals requires dam, and explain the proof each side uses.

Core Idea
Delaying a Hajj ritual from its time or place triggers dam according to Abu Hanifa, not according to Sahibayn.

This passage addresses a key intra-Hanafi dispute: does delaying or rearranging Hajj rituals require an additional sacrifice? The answer depends on whether one follows Imam Abu Hanifa or his two foremost students. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to identify when a wajib penalty applies and when simple makeup (qada) suffices.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Note the specific cases: delaying shaving, tawaf ziyarah, stoning, and advancing one ritual over another (e.g., shaving before stoning).
The passage covers both ta'khir (delay) and taqdim (advancement).
2
State Imam Abu Hanifa's position
Imam Abu Hanifa rules that dam is wajib in all these cases. His evidence is a hadith and qiyas on place- and time-bound rituals.
The hadith: 'Whoever advances one ritual over another owes dam.'
3
State the Sahibayn's position
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold that no dam is required; only qada (making up) of the missed ritual is needed. Their analogy is to missed prayers, where only qada is required.
They argue that any missed act in Hajj is compensated by qada alone.
4
Analyze each proof
Compare the proofs: Imam Abu Hanifa relies on a specific hadith and qiyas on the miqat case; the Sahibayn rely on a general qiyas to prayer. Evaluate which carries more weight in Hanafi usul.
A direct nass (hadith) generally overrides qiyas.
5
Determine the practical consequence
The thamarah al-khilaf: in any case of delay/advancement, a pilgrim following Abu Hanifa must offer a sacrifice; following Sahibayn, no sacrifice is needed.
The mufta bihi in the school tends toward Abu Hanifa, but the text does not explicitly state this.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
کتاب الحج
۱۲/۱۱، ذی الحجہ گذر گئے اور نہ سر منڈایا اور نہ قصر کیا تو امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک اس پر ایک قربانی واجب ہوگی ۔ اور اسی طرح جب اتر ، نے طواف زیارت کو مؤخر کر دیا تو قربانی واجب ہوگی۔ لیکن صاحبین کے نزدیک مذکورہ دونوں صورتوں میں قربانی واجب نہیں ہے۔ اور امام صاحب اور صاحبین کے درمیان یہی اختلاف اس وقت ہے جبکہ جمرہ عقبہ کی رمی کو یوم تحریعنی دسویں ذی الحجہ سے گیارہویں تک مؤخر کر دیا اور گیارہویں کی رمی کو بارہویں تک اور بارہویں کی رمی کو تیرہویں تک اور تیرہویں کی رمی کو چودہویں تک مؤخر کر دیا تو امام اعظم کے نزدیک اس تاخیر کی وجہ سے دم واجب ہوگا اور صاحبین کے نزدیک واجب نہ ہوگا۔ اور اگر حج کے ایک نسک کو دوسرے نسک پر مقدم کر دیا مثلاً حلق کو رمی جمار پر مقدم کر دیا ، یا قارن یا مستمتع نے دم تمتع کو رمی سے پہلے ذبح کر دیا یا محرم نے ذبح سے پہلے حلق کرا لیا تو ان سب صورتوں میں امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک دم جنایت واجب ہوگا ۔ اور صاحبین کے نزدیک واجب نہ ہوگا ۔ صاحبین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ جو چیز اپنے وقت سے فوت ہو جاتی ہے اس کی تلافی قضاء کے ساتھ کی جاتی ہے اور جس چیز کی تلافی قضاء سے کی جائے اس میں قضا کے علاوہ اور کوئی دوسری چیز واجب نہیں ہوتی جیسا کہ احکام شرع کے تتبع سے معلوم ہوتا ہے۔ مثلاً نماز کی قضاء کے ساتھ اور کوئی کفارہ وغیرہ واجب نہیں ہوتا۔ اسی طرح مسائل حج میں بھی جب کسی نسک کی قضاء کرلی گئی تو محض تاخیر کی وجہ سے قضاء کے علاوہ دم وغیر ہ واجب نہ ہوگا۔ امام ابوحنیفہ کی دلیل حدیث ابن مسعود ہے اور بعض نسخوں میں ابن مسعود کے بجائے ابن عباس کا ذکر ہے حدیث یہ ہے کہ جس نے ایک نسک کو دوسرے نسک پر مقدم کیا تو اسپر دم واجب ہے۔ دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ جو نسک کسی مکان کے ساتھ خاص ہو اس کو اگر اس مکان سے مؤخر کر دیا گیا تو اس پر دم واجب ہوتا ہے جیسے حاجی اگر بغیر احرام کے میقات سے گذر گیا اور پھر احرام باندھا تو اس پر دم واجب ہو گا۔ اسی طرح جو نسک کسی زمانہ کے ساتھ خاص وہ اس کو اگر اس زمانہ سے مؤخر کر دیا جائے تو اس پر بھی دم واجب ہوگا ۔ ان دونوں کے درمیان جامع تاخیر کے نقصان کا پیدا ہوتا ہے۔
The Book of Hajj. If the 12th/11th of Dhul-Hijjah passed and he did not shave or shorten [his hair], then according to Imam Abu Hanifa one sacrifice becomes obligatory upon him. Similarly, when he delayed Tawaf al-Ziyarah, then sacrifice becomes obligatory. But according to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), in both mentioned cases sacrifice is not obligatory. And this same difference between Imam and the Sahibayn is when the stoning of Jamrat al-Aqabah is delayed from the Day of Nahr (10th Dhul-Hijjah) to the 11th, and the stoning of the 11th is delayed to the 12th, and the stoning of the 12th is delayed to the 13th, and the stoning of the 13th is delayed to the 14th; then according to Abu Hanifa, due to this delay, dam becomes obligatory, and according to the Sahibayn it is not obligatory. And if one ritual (nusk) of Hajj is advanced over another, e.g., shaving is advanced over stoning the jamarat, or a qarin or mutamatti' performs the sacrifice of tamattu' before stoning, or a muhrim shaves before sacrificing, then in all these cases according to Imam Abu Hanifa, dam janayat becomes obligatory, and according to the Sahibayn it is not obligatory. The proof of the Sahibayn is that what misses its time is compensated by qada (making up), and what is compensated by qada, no other thing besides qada is obligatory, as is known from following the rulings of Shariah. For example, with qada of prayer, no other expiation etc. is obligatory. Similarly in Hajj issues, when qada of a ritual is performed, then mere delay does not obligate dam or anything else besides qada. The proof of Imam Abu Hanifa is the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud, and in some copies Ibn Abbas is mentioned; the hadith is that whoever advances one ritual over another, dam is obligatory upon him. Another proof is that a ritual which is specific to a place, if it is delayed from that place, then dam is obligatory, like if a pilgrim passes the miqat without ihram and then puts on ihram, then dam becomes obligatory. Similarly, a ritual which is specific to a time, if it is delayed from that time, then dam also becomes obligatory. Between these two, the common factor is that harm of delay occurs.
Source pages p. 446

Commentary
This passage discusses the legal ruling on delaying Hajj rituals and the consequential obligation of dam (sacrifice) according to the Hanafi school. The author first presents the positions: Imam Abu Hanifa holds that delaying rituals such as shaving, tawaf ziyarah, or stoning beyond their prescribed times or places necessitates dam, while the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) disagree and consider no dam required. The dispute extends to cases where rituals are performed out of order (taqdim). The Sahibayn argue from the general principle that when an act is missed and then made up (qada), no additional penalty is needed, analogous to missed prayers. Imam Abu Hanifa relies on a hadith (from Ibn Mas'ud or Ibn Abbas) that whoever advances one ritual over another owes dam, and also on qiyas: rituals tied to a specific place or time, when delayed from that place or time, necessitate dam—like the case of passing the miqat without ihram. The commonality is the harm caused by delay. The passage is primarily an intra-madhhab dispute within the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
دم (dam): A sacrifice (usually a sheep or goat) obligatory as compensation for certain violations in Hajj/Umrah.
نسک (nusk): A ritual act of Hajj or Umrah, such as rami, halq, tawaf, sa'y, etc.
قضاء (qada): Making up a missed obligatory act by performing it later.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, what is the ruling on delaying the stoning of Jamrat al-Aqabah from the 10th to the 11th of Dhul-Hijjah?
A) It is permissible with no penalty
B) Dam becomes wajib
C) Qada is required but no dam
D) The Hajj is invalid

Key Takeaway
Imam Abu Hanifa requires dam for any delay or advancement of Hajj rituals; the Sahibayn hold that qada suffices.

Shaving Outside the Haram and Obligation of Dam
Dispute on whether halq/qasr outside Haram necessitates dam

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four Hanafi positions on whether halq/qasr outside the Haram necessitates dam, and apply the qiyas of halq to salam to evaluate the proofs.

Core Idea
Shaving outside the Haram triggers dam according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, but not according to Abu Yusuf – the dispute hinges on whether halq is restricted to the Haram.

This passage from al-Hidayah presents a classic intra-Hanafi debate about the obligation of dam when a pilgrim shaves or shortens hair outside the sacred precincts of the Haram. The core question is whether the ritual of halq is bound by place (Haram) and time (days of Nahr) such that violating these restrictions necessitates compensation. You will encounter four distinct positions from the early Hanafi masters, each supported by textual and analogical arguments.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its legal consequence
The passage discusses two scenarios: a pilgrim shaving during the days of Nahr outside the Haram, and a Umrah performer shortening hair after leaving the Haram. The legal consequence is whether dam (a sacrificial offering) becomes wajib.
2
State the four Hanafi positions
Abu Hanifa: halq is restricted by both time (days of Nahr) and place (Haram). Muhammad: restricted by place only. Zufar: restricted by time only. Abu Yusuf: restricted by neither. These lead to differing rulings on dam.
Abu Hanifa and Muhammad agree on dam for place violation; Abu Yusuf says no dam ever; Zufar says dam only if time violated.
3
Analyze the proofs of Abu Yusuf
Abu Yusuf cites the incident of Hudaybiyyah where the Prophet and Companions shaved outside the Haram. This shows halq is not exclusive to the Haram.
Hudaybiyyah is generally considered outside the Haram, though the opponents argue part of it may be inside.
4
Analyze the proofs of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad
They use qiyas: halq is a ritual that makes one halal (muhallil), similar to the salam at the end of prayer. Salam is a wajib of prayer even though it ends it; similarly, halq is a wajib of ihram. As a ritual, it becomes specific to the Haram, like slaughter (dhabh).
The analogy rests on the idea that a ritual act of exit is bound by the sacred space.
5
Determine the mufta bihi and practical consequence
The text states 'al-asah' (the more correct) is that it is disputed, but the weight is with Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. The mufta bihi is that dam is wajib for halq outside the Haram.
The thamarah al-khilaf: a pilgrim shaving in Jeddah owes dam according to the relied-upon view; according to Abu Yusuf, nothing.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ایام النحر میں حرم کے علاوہ حلق کیا تو دم لازم ہے، عمرہ کیا اور حرم سے نکل کر قصر
کیا تو دم واجب ہے، اقوال فقہاء
فَإِنْ حَلَقَ فِي أَيَّامِ النَّحْرِ فِى غَيْرِ الْحَرَمِ فَعَلَيْهِ دَمُ وَمَنِ اعْتَمَرَ فَخَرَجَ مِنَ الْحَرَمِ وَ قَصَرَ فَعَلَيْهِ دَمُ عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيْفَةَ وَ مُحَمَّدٍ وَ قَالَ أَبُو يُوسُفَ لَا شَى عَلَيْهِ قَالَ ذَكَرَ فِى الْجَامِعِ الصَّغِيرِ قولُ أَبِى يُوسُفَ فِى الْمُعْتَمِر وَلَمْ يَذْكُرْ فِى الحاج وَقِيلَ هُوَ بِالْإِنْفَاقِ لأنَّ السُّنَّةَ جَرَتْ فِي الْحَجِ بِالْخَلْقِ بِمِنى وَهُوَ مِنَ الْحَرَمِ وَالْأَصَحُ أَنَّهُ عَلَى الْخِلَافِ هُوَ يَقُولُ اَلْحَلْقَ غَيْرُ مُختَصّ بِالْحَرَم لأنَّ النَّبِيَّ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ وَأَصْحَابَهُ أحْصِرُ وَ بِالْحُدَيْبِيَّةِ وَحَلَقُوا فِي غَيْرِ الْحَرَمِ وَلَهُمَا اَنَّ الْحَلْقَ لَمَا جُعِلَ مُحَلّلاً صَارَ كَالسَّلَام فِي آخِرِ الصَّلوة فَإِنَّهُ مِنْ وَاجِبَاتِهَا وَإِنْ كَانَ مُحَلَّلًا فَإِذَا صَارَ نُسُكَا اِخْتَصَّ بِالحَرَمِ كَالذَّبْحِ وَبَعْضُ الْحُدَنِيَّةِ مِنَ الْحَرَمِ فَلَعَلَّهُمْ خَلَقُوا فِيهِ فَالْحَاصِلُ أَنَّ الْحَلْقَ يَتَوَفَّتُ بِالزَّمَانِ وَالْمَكَانَ عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةً وَعِندَ أبى يُوسُفَ لَا يَتَوَفَّتُ بِهِمَا وَعِنْدَ مُحَمَّدٍ يَتَوَفَّتُ بِالْمَكَانِ دُونَ الزَّمَانِ وَعِندَ زُفَرَ يَتَوَفَّتْ بِالزَّمَانِ دُونَ الْمَكَانِ وَهَذَا الْخِلَافُ فِى التوقِيْتِ فِى حَقِّ التَّضْمِيْنِ بِالدَّمِ أَمَا لَا يَتَوَقَّتُ في حق التحلل بالاتفاق ترجمہ پس اگر ایا منجر میں حرم کے علاوہ میں حلق کیا تو اس پر دم واجب ہے اور جس نے عمرہ کیا پھر حرم سے نکل گیا اور قصر کیا تو اس پر بھی
دم ہے ( یہ حکم ) طرفین کے نزدیک ہے اور ابو یوسف نے فرمایا کہ اس پر کچھ واجب نہیں ہے۔ مصنف نے کہا کہ امام محمد نے جامع صغیر میں ابو یوسف کا قول عمرہ ادا کرنے والے کے حق میں ذکر کیا ہے۔ اور حج کرنے والے کے حق میں ذکر نہیں کیا اور کہا گیا کہ یہ بالا تفاق ہے کیونکہ حج کے اندرمنی میں حلق کرنے کی سنت جاری ہے اور منی حرم میں سے ہے۔ اور اصح یہ ہے کہ یہ مختلف فیہ ہے۔ ابو یوسف فرماتے ہیں کہ حلق کرنا حرم کے ساتھ خاص نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم اور آپ کے صحابہ حدیبیہ میں روک دیئے گئے اور انہوں نے حرم سے با ہر حلق کیا اور طرفین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ حلق کرنا جب احرام سے حلال کرنے والا قرار دیا گیا تو وہ نماز کے آخر میں سلام کے مانند ہو گیا۔ کیونکہ سلام بھی نماز کے واجبات میں سے ہے اگر چہ تحریمہ نماز سے حلال کرنے والا ہے۔ پس جب حلق نسک ہے تو حرم کے ساتھ خاص ہوگا ۔ جیسے ذبح کرنا اور حدیبیہ کا کچھ حصہ حرم میں داخل ہے بہت ممکن ہے کہ ان حضرات نے اسی میں حلق کیا ہو۔ حاصل یہ کہ امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک حلق کرنا زمان و مکان دونوں کے ساتھ موقت ہے اور امام ابو یوسف کے نزدیک دونوں کے ساتھ موقت نہیں ہے اور امام محمد کے نزدیک مکان کے ساتھ موقت ہے لیکن زمان کے ساتھ موقت نہیں ہے۔ اور امام زفر کے نزدیک زمان کے ساتھ موقت ہے نہ کہ مکان
کے ساتھ اور یہ توقیت میں اختلاف دم کا ضمان لازم ہونے کے حق میں ہے۔ رہا حلال ہونے کے حق میں تو بالا تفاق موقت نہیں ہے۔ تشریح اس عبارت میں دو مسئلوں کا حکم مذکور ہے۔ پہلا مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ حاجی نے ایام نحر میں حرم سے با ہر حلق کرایا۔ دوسرا مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ ایک شخص نے عمرہ ادا کیا یعنی طواف اور سعی کی پھر وہ حرم سے باہر چلا گیا اور قصر کیا یعنی بال کترے تو طرفین کے نز دیکھ ان دونوں صورتوں میں دم واجب ہوگا۔ اور امام ابو یوسف نے فرمایا کہ اس پر کچھ واجب نہ ہوگا۔ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ جامع صغیر میں امام محمد نے ابو یوسف کا قول لَا شَيْءٍ عَلَيْهِ ۔ عمرہ ادا کرنے والے کے حق میں ذکر کیا ہے۔ اور حاجی کے حق میں ذکر نہیں کیا ہے۔ یعنی امام ابو یوسف کے نزدیک اگر عمرہ ادا کرنے والے نے حرم سے باہر جا کر قصر کرایا تو اس پر دم واجب نہیں ہو گا لیکن اگر حاجی نے حرم سے باہر حلق کرایا تو اس بارے میں امام محمد نے جامع صغیر میں امام ابو یوسف کی نسبت سے کچھ ذکر نہیں کیا نہ یہ ذکر کیا کہ ابو یوسف کے نزدیک اسپر بھی دم واجب ہوگا اور نہ یہ ذکر کیا کہ اس پر دم واجب نہیں ہو گا بعض حضرات نے فرمایا ہے کہ حاجی کے حرم سے باہر حلق کرانے کی صورت میں بالا تفاق دم واجب ہو گا طرفین کے نزدیک بھی اور ابو یوسف کے نزدیک بھی ۔ کیونکہ حج کے اندر رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم ، صحابہ اور تابعین اور بعد کے مسلمانوں کی یہی سنت رہی ہے کہ وہ منی میں حلق کراتے تھے اور منی حرم ہی کا ایک حصہ ہے۔ پس اس توارث سے ثابت ہوا کہ حرم کے اندر حلق کرانا واجب ہے اور جب حرم کے اندر حلق کرانا واجب ہوا تو حرم سے باہر حلق کرانا موجب دم ہوگا ۔ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ جس طرح عمرہ ادا کرنے والے کے حرم سے باہر حلق کرانے کی صورت میں وجوب دم اور عدم وجوب دم میں طرفین اور ابو یوسف کا اختلاف ہے اسی طرح اگر حاجی نے حرم سے باہر حلق کرایا تو وہ بھی مختلف فیہ ہے۔ چنانچہ طرفین کے نزدیک اس پر دم واجب ہوگا اور ابو یوسف کے نزدیک دم واجب نہیں ہوگا۔ امام ابو یوسف کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ حلق کرانا حرم کے ساتھ مختص نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم اور آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم کے صحابہ جب حدیبیہ میں روک دیئے گئے تو ان حضرات نے حدیبیہ ہی میں حلق کرایا اور حدیبیہ حرم سے باہر ہے تو گویا ان حضرات نے حرم سے باہر حلق کرایا اور جب رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم اور صحابہ نے حرم سے باہر حلق کرایا تو معلوم ہوا کہ حلق حرم کے ساتھ خاص نہیں ہے۔ اور جب حلق حرم کے ساتھ خاص نہیں ہے تو کسی واجب کا ترک بھی نہیں پایا گیا اور جب واجب ترک نہیں ہوا تو دم واجب نہ ہوگا۔ طرفین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ جس طرح
If he shaved during the days of Nahr outside the Haram, then dam is obligatory. And whoever performed Umrah and went out of the Haram and shortened [his hair], then dam is obligatory according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. And Abu Yusuf said: nothing is upon him. [The author] said: He [Imam Muhammad] mentioned in al-Jami' al-Saghir the saying of Abu Yusuf regarding the one performing Umrah, and he did not mention regarding the Hajj. And it was said that this is unanimous because the sunnah in Hajj has been shaving at Mina, and it is part of the Haram. And the correct view is that it is disputed. He [Abu Yusuf] says: Shaving is not specific to the Haram because the Prophet (peace be upon him) and his Companions were confined at Hudaybiyyah and they shaved outside the Haram. And for them [Abu Hanifa and Muhammad] the proof is that shaving, when it is made a means of becoming halal, becomes like the salam at the end of prayer, for it is among its wajibat, even though it makes halal. So when it becomes a ritual, it becomes specific to the Haram like slaughter. And part of Hudaybiyyah is within the Haram; perhaps they shaved there. The conclusion is that shaving is restricted by time and place according to Abu Hanifa, according to Abu Yusuf it is restricted by neither, according to Muhammad it is restricted by place but not time, and according to Zufar it is restricted by time but not place. And this difference regarding restriction is concerning the liability of dam. As for becoming halal, it is unanimously not restricted. Commentary: In this passage, the ruling of two issues is mentioned. First: a pilgrim shaved outside the Haram during the days of Nahr. Second: a person performed Umrah (tawaf and sa'y) then left the Haram and shortened his hair. According to the two [Abu Hanifa and Muhammad], dam is obligatory in both cases. Imam Abu Yusuf said that nothing is obligatory. The author of al-Hidayah says that Imam Muhammad in al-Jami' al-Saghir mentioned Abu Yusuf's statement regarding the one performing Umrah, and did not mention regarding the Hajj. Some said that this is unanimous because in Hajj the sunnah is to shave at Mina, which is part of the Haram. But the correct view is that it is disputed. Imam Abu Yusuf's proof is that shaving is not exclusive to the Haram because the Prophet and his Companions when confined at Hudaybiyyah shaved there, and Hudaybiyyah is outside the Haram. The two [Abu Hanifa and Muhammad] argue that shaving, being a means of exiting ihram, is like the salam in prayer—it is a wajib even if it makes halal. So when it becomes a ritual, it becomes specific to the Haram like slaughter. And part of Hudaybiyyah is within the Haram; perhaps they shaved there. The outcome is that shaving is time- and place-bound according to Abu Hanifa; according to Abu Yusuf it is bound to neither; according to Muhammad it is bound to place but not time; according to Zufar it is bound to time but not place. This dispute about restriction is concerning liability of dam. As for becoming halal, it is unanimously not restricted.
Source pages p. 446

Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling on shaving (halq) or shortening (qasr) hair outside the Haram during Hajj or Umrah, and whether this necessitates dam. The author first states the general rule in Arabic: shaving outside the Haram during the days of Nahr requires dam, and performing Umrah and then shortening hair outside the Haram also requires dam according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. Abu Yusuf says nothing is required. The text then examines a nuance: Imam Muhammad in al-Jami' al-Saghir only reported Abu Yusuf's view for the Umrah case, not for the Hajj. Some scholars thought there was consensus for the Hajj case because the established practice is to shave at Mina (inside Haram), but the correct view is that it is disputed. The proofs: Abu Yusuf relies on the incident of Hudaybiyyah where the Prophet and Companions shaved outside the Haram, proving that halq is not exclusive to the Haram. The other two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) use qiyas: halq is a ritual that makes one halal, similar to the final salam in prayer which is a wajib even though it concludes the prayer. As a ritual, it becomes specific to the Haram like slaughter. They also argue that part of Hudaybiyyah might be within the Haram. The discussion then summarizes the positions of four Hanafi imams on the restriction of halq by time and place: Abu Hanifa: restricted by both time (days of Nahr) and place (Haram); Abu Yusuf: restricted by neither; Muhammad: restricted by place only; Zufar: restricted by time only. Importantly, this restriction only affects the liability for dam; as for becoming halal, halq is not restricted and is valid regardless of time and place. The commentary clarifies that the dispute concerns the need for dam when halq is done outside the Haram, not the validity of the halq itself.

Key Terms
حلق (halq): Shaving the head, a ritual of exiting ihram during Hajj/Umrah.
توقیت (tawqit): Restriction to a specific time or place for the obligation of dam.
تضمن (tadmin): Liability, specifically the obligation to pay dam as compensation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Muhammad (al-Shaybani), what is the restriction of halq that determines dam?
A) Restricted by both time and place
B) Restricted by place only
C) Restricted by time only
D) Restricted by neither time nor place

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school features a rich internal debate on the spatial and temporal restrictions of halq, but the operative position is that shaving outside the Haram necessitates a dam.

Hajj — Pilgrimage

Halq Outside Haram During Hajj: The Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Dam
Intra-Hanafi dispute on dam for halq outside Haram during Hajj

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding dam for shaving outside the Haram during Hajj, state the evidence of each side, and identify the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf).

Core Idea
Halq outside the Haram during Hajj: Abu Hanifa and Muhammad say dam wajib; Abu Yusuf says no dam; the dispute hinges on whether halq is muwaqqat bi al-makan wa al-zaman.

This lesson unpacks a classic intra-Hanafi dispute from Al-Hidayah. The question: if a pilgrim shaves his head outside the boundaries of the Haram during the days of Nahr, is a dam required? Imam Abu Hanifa, Imam Muhammad, and Imam Zufar each have different views on whether shaving is restricted by time and place, while Imam Abu Yusuf holds it is not restricted at all. We will trace the evidence—from the incident at Hudaybiyya to the analogy with salam in prayer—and understand why the author of Al-Hidayah concludes that the issue is disputed (mukhtalaf fih).

Guided Path
1
Identify the core issue
The issue is whether halq (shaving the head) is specifically required to be performed within the Haram and during the days of Nahr, such that violating either requires a dam (compensatory sacrifice).
2
State the positions of the four Hanafi imams
List: Abu Hanifa: restricted by both time and place → dam if either violated. Abu Yusuf: not restricted → no dam ever. Muhammad: restricted by place only → dam if outside Haram. Zufar: restricted by time only → dam if outside days of Nahr.
3
Analyze Abu Yusuf's evidence
The Prophet (ﷺ) and Companions shaved at Hudaybiyya, which is outside the Haram, proving halq is not specific to Haram.
4
Analyze the opposing evidence (tarafayn)
Qiyas to salam in prayer: both are wajibat that conclude the ritual; all rituals of Hajj are specific to Haram (like dhabh). Also, continuous practice of shaving in Mina. Response: Hudaybiyya may have part inside Haram.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf and note the consensus on exiting ihram
The dispute is only about dam, not about the validity of exiting ihram (halal by consensus). Practical: followers of each imam act accordingly.
The author of Al-Hidayah states that the correct view is that it is disputed (mukhtalaf fih).

ہے اور امام محمد کے نزدیک مکان کے ساتھ موقت ہے لیکن زمان کے ساتھ موقت نہیں ہے۔ اور امام زفر کے نزدیک زمان کے ساتھ موقت ہے نہ کہ مکان کے ساتھ اور یہ توقیت میں اختلاف دم کا ضمان لازم ہونے کے حق میں ہے۔ رہا حلال ہونے کے حق میں تو بالا تفاق موقت نہیں ہے۔ تشریح اس عبارت میں دو مسئلوں کا حکم مذکور ہے۔ پہلا مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ حاجی نے ایام نحر میں حرم سے با ہر حلق کرایا۔ دوسرا مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ ایک شخص نے عمرہ ادا کیا یعنی طواف اور سعی کی پھر وہ حرم سے باہر چلا گیا اور قصر کیا یعنی بال کترے تو طرفین کے نز دیکھ ان دونوں صورتوں میں دم واجب ہوگا۔ اور امام ابو یوسف نے فرمایا کہ اس پر کچھ واجب نہ ہوگا۔ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ جامع صغیر میں امام محمد نے ابو یوسف کا قول لَا شَيْءٍ عَلَيْهِ ۔ عمرہ ادا کرنے والے کے حق میں ذکر کیا ہے۔ اور حاجی کے حق میں ذکر نہیں کیا ہے۔ یعنی امام ابو یوسف کے نزدیک اگر عمرہ ادا کرنے والے نے حرم سے باہر جا کر قصر کرایا تو اس پر دم واجب نہیں ہو گا لیکن اگر حاجی نے حرم سے باہر حلق کرایا تو اس بارے میں امام محمد نے جامع صغیر میں امام ابو یوسف کی نسبت سے کچھ ذکر نہیں کیا نہ یہ ذکر کیا کہ ابو یوسف کے نزدیک اسپر بھی دم واجب ہوگا اور نہ یہ ذکر کیا کہ اس پر دم واجب نہیں ہو گا بعض حضرات نے فرمایا ہے کہ حاجی کے حرم سے باہر حلق کرانے کی صورت میں بالا تفاق دم واجب ہو گا طرفین کے نزدیک بھی اور ابو یوسف کے نزدیک بھی ۔ کیونکہ حج کے اندر رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم ، صحابہ اور تابعین اور بعد کے مسلمانوں کی یہی سنت رہی ہے کہ وہ منی میں حلق کراتے تھے اور منی حرم ہی کا ایک حصہ ہے۔ پس اس توارث سے ثابت ہوا کہ حرم کے اندر حلق کرانا واجب ہے اور جب حرم کے اندر حلق کرانا واجب ہوا تو حرم سے باہر حلق کرانا موجب دم ہوگا ۔ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ جس طرح عمرہ ادا کرنے والے کے حرم سے باہر حلق کرانے کی صورت میں وجوب دم اور عدم وجوب دم میں طرفین اور ابو یوسف کا اختلاف ہے اسی طرح اگر حاجی نے حرم سے باہر حلق کرایا تو وہ بھی مختلف فیہ ہے۔ چنانچہ طرفین کے نزدیک اس پر دم واجب ہوگا اور ابو یوسف کے نزدیک دم واجب نہیں ہوگا۔ امام ابو یوسف کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ حلق کرانا حرم کے ساتھ مختص نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم اور آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم کے صحابہ جب حدیبیہ میں روک دیئے گئے تو ان حضرات نے حدیبیہ ہی میں حلق کرایا اور حدیبیہ حرم سے باہر ہے تو گویا ان حضرات نے حرم سے باہر حلق کرایا اور جب رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم اور صحابہ نے حرم سے باہر حلق کرایا تو معلوم ہوا کہ حلق حرم کے ساتھ خاص نہیں ہے۔ اور جب حلق حرم کے ساتھ خاص نہیں ہے تو کسی واجب کا ترک بھی نہیں پایا گیا اور جب واجب ترک نہیں ہوا تو دم واجب نہ ہوگا۔ طرفین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ جس طرح سلام واجبات نماز میں سے ہے اگر چہ تحریمہ نماز سے حلال کرنے والال یعنی نکالنے والا ہے اسی طرح حلق بھی واجبات حج میں سے ہے اگر چہ وہ احرام سے نکالنے والا ہے پس جب حلق واجبات حج میں سے ہے تو وہ مناسک حج میں سے ایک نشکک ہوا اور مناسک حج تمام کے تمام حرم کے ساتھ مختص ہیں جیسے ذبح کرنا وغیرہ۔ تو حلق بھی حرم کے ساتھ مختص ہوگا اور جب حلق حرم کے ساتھ مختص ہے تو حرم کے اندر حلق کرانا واجب ہوگا ۔ پس جب حاجی نے حرم سے باہر حلق کرایا تو وہ تارک واجب ہوا اور تارک واجب پر دم واجب ہوتا ہے اس لئے اس پر دم واجب ہوگا اور ابو یوسف کا یہ کہنا کہ اللہ کے رسول صلى الله عليه وسلم اور آپ کے صحابہ نے حدیبیہ میں حلق کیا ہے اور حدیبیہ حرم سے باہر ہے غلط ہے۔ کیونکہ حدیبیہ کا کچھ حصہ حرم کے اندر داخل ہے۔ پس ممکن ہے کہ ان حضرات نے اسی حصہ میں حلق کیا ہو۔ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ حاصل یہ ہے کہ حج کے اندر حلق امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک زمان اور مکان دونوں کے ساتھ مختص ہے زمان سے ایام نحر اور مکان سے حرم مراد ہے یعنی ایام نحر اور حرم میں حلق کرانا ضروری ہے۔ چنانچہ اگر ایام نحر کے بعد حرم کے اندر حلق کیا تو بھی امام صاحب کے نزدیک دم واجب ہوگا اور اگر حرم سے باہر ایام نحر میں حلق کیا تب بھی دم واجب ہوگا۔ اور ابو یوسف کے نزدیک زمان ومکان دونوں کے ساتھ مختص نہیں ہے۔ چنانچہ اگر ایام نحر کے علاوہ میں حلق کرایا یا حرم کے علاوہ میں حلق کرایا تو دونوں صورتوں میں دم واجب نہ ہو گا۔ اور امام محمد کے نزدیک مکان یعنی حرم کے ساتھ تو خاص ہے مگر زمانہ یعنی ایام نحر کے ساتھ خاص نہیں ہے۔ چنانچہ اگر حرم کے با ہر حلق کیا تو امام محمد کے نزدیک دم واجب ہوگا اور اگر ایام نحر گذر نے کے بعد حلق کیا تو دم واجب نہ ہوگا۔ اور امام زفر کے نزدیک زمانہ کے ساتھ تو خاص ہے مگر مکان کے ساتھ خاص نہیں ہے چنانچہ اگر حاجی نے ایام نحر کے بعد حلق کرایا تو امام زفر کے نزدیک اس پر دم واجب ہو گا لیکن اگر حرم کے باہر حلق کرایا تو دم واجب نہ ہوگا۔ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ توقیت کا یہ اختلاف دم واجب ہونے کے حق میں ہے یعنی اگر حلق اس کے علاوہ میں کرایا جس کے ساتھ موقت کیا تھا تو جو حضرات موقت کرتے ہیں ان کے نزدیک دم واجب ہوگا اور جو حضرات موقت نہیں کرتے ان کے نزدیک دم واجب نہ ہوگا ۔ احترام سے نکل جانے کے حق میں بالا تفاق موقت نہیں ہے حتی کہ جہاں کہیں حلق کرے گا بالا تفاق احرام سے نکل جائے گا۔ لیکن جس نے اس کو حرم اور زمانہ سے موقت کیا اس کے نزدیک خلاف کرنے سے دم لازم ہوگا۔ اور جس نے موقت نہیں کیا اس کے نزدیک حلال ہو گیا اور کچھ لا زم بھی نہیں ہوگا۔ واللہ اعلم بالصواب۔ جمیل احمد غفرلہ
There is a dam (this ruling) according to the two sides (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), and Abu Yusuf said that nothing is obligatory upon him. The author said that Imam Muhammad mentioned Abu Yusuf's statement in al-Jami' al-Saghir regarding the one performing Umrah, and did not mention it regarding the one performing Hajj. It was said that this is by consensus because in Hajj there is an ongoing sunnah of shaving in Mina, and Mina is part of the Haram. But the most correct is that it is disputed. Abu Yusuf says that shaving is not specific to the Haram because the Messenger of Allah (ﷺ) and his Companions were detained at Hudaybiyya and they shaved outside the Haram. The two sides' evidence is that when shaving is made the cause of exiting ihram, it becomes like the salam at the end of prayer, because salam is among the wajibat of prayer even though it is what exits the prayer. So when shaving is a ritual (nusk), it will be specific to the Haram, like slaughtering. And part of Hudaybiyya is inside the Haram; it is very possible that those people shaved in that part. The summary is that according to Imam Abu Hanifa, shaving is restricted by both time and place; according to Imam Abu Yusuf, it is not restricted by either; according to Imam Muhammad, it is restricted by place but not time; according to Imam Zufar, it is restricted by time but not place. This difference in restriction is regarding the guarantee of dam. As for becoming halal (exiting ihram), it is not restricted by consensus. Commentary: In this phrase, the ruling of two issues is mentioned. First issue: A pilgrim shaved outside the Haram during the days of Nahr. Second issue: A person performed Umrah (tawaf and sa'i), then left the Haram and trimmed his hair. According to the two sides, in both cases dam is obligatory. And Imam Abu Yusuf said that nothing is obligatory upon him. The author of al-Hidayah says that in al-Jami' al-Saghir, Imam Muhammad mentioned Abu Yusuf's statement "there is nothing upon him" regarding the one performing Umrah, and did not mention it regarding the pilgrim. Meaning, according to Abu Yusuf, if the one performing Umrah left the Haram and trimmed, no dam is obligatory; but if the pilgrim shaved outside the Haram, Imam Muhammad did not mention anything from Abu Yusuf regarding this. Some have said that in the case of the pilgrim shaving outside the Haram, dam is obligatory by consensus, even according to Abu Yusuf, because in Hajj the continuous practice of the Messenger of Allah (ﷺ), the Companions, the Followers, and later Muslims was to shave in Mina, and Mina is part of the Haram. So by this transmission it is established that shaving inside the Haram is obligatory, and when shaving inside the Haram is obligatory, then shaving outside the Haram necessitates dam. The author of al-Hidayah says that just as there is a difference between the two sides and Abu Yusuf regarding the obligation or non-obligation of dam when the Umrah performer shaves outside the Haram, similarly if the pilgrim shaves outside the Haram, it is also disputed. Thus, according to the two sides, dam is obligatory upon him; according to Abu Yusuf, dam is not obligatory. Abu Yusuf's evidence is that shaving is not specific to the Haram because the Messenger of Allah (ﷺ) and his Companions when detained at Hudaybiyya, they shaved there, and Hudaybiyya is outside the Haram. So it indicates that shaving is not specific to the Haram. And when it is not specific, there is no omission of an obligatory act, so no dam is required. The two sides' evidence is that just as salam is among the wajibat of prayer even though it exits the prayer, similarly shaving is among the wajibat of Hajj even though it exits ihram. So when shaving is among the wajibat of Hajj, it becomes one of the rituals of Hajj, and all rituals of Hajj are specific to the Haram, like slaughtering. Therefore shaving is also specific to the Haram. And when it is specific, shaving inside the Haram is obligatory. So when the pilgrim shaves outside the Haram, he becomes one who omits an obligatory act, and on the one who omits an obligatory act, dam is obligatory. Therefore dam is obligatory upon him. Abu Yusuf's statement that the Messenger of Allah (ﷺ) and his Companions shaved at Hudaybiyya and Hudaybiyya is outside the Haram is incorrect, because part of Hudaybiyya is inside the Haram. So it is possible that those people shaved in that part. The author of al-Hidayah says that the summary is that in Hajj, shaving according to Imam Abu Hanifa is specific to both time and place: time means the days of Nahr, place means the Haram. So if one shaves inside the Haram after the days of Nahr, dam is still obligatory according to him; and if one shaves outside the Haram during the days of Nahr, dam is also obligatory. According to Abu Yusuf, it is not specific to either time or place: if one shaves outside the days of Nahr or outside the Haram, no dam is obligatory. According to Imam Muhammad, it is specific to place (the Haram) but not time: if one shaves outside the Haram, dam is obligatory according to him; if one shaves after the days of Nahr, no dam is obligatory. According to Imam Zufar, it is specific to time but not place: if one shaves after the days of Nahr, dam is obligatory according to him; but if one shaves outside the Haram, no dam is obligatory. The author of al-Hidayah says that this difference in restriction is regarding the obligation of dam: if shaving is performed in a manner contrary to what it is restricted to, then according to those who restrict it, dam is obligatory; according to those who do not restrict it, no dam is obligatory. As for exiting ihram, it is not restricted by consensus, such that wherever one shaves, he will exit ihram by consensus. But those who restrict it to the Haram and time, violation necessitates dam; those who do not restrict it, the person becomes halal and nothing is required. And Allah knows best what is correct. Jameel Ahmad, may Allah forgive him.
Source pages p. 447

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah is an intra-Hanafi dispute (ikhtilaf) regarding whether a dam (sacrificial animal) is obligatory on a pilgrim (haji) who shaves his head (halq) or trims his hair (qasr) outside the boundaries of the Haram during the days of Nahr (10th-12th of Dhul Hijjah). The debate centers on whether the act of halq is 'muwaqqat' (restricted/specified) by place (Haram) and/or time (days of Nahr). The text first presents the basic ruling: according to the 'tarafayn' (the two sides, i.e., Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani), dam is obligatory; according to Imam Abu Yusuf, nothing is obligatory. The author notes that Imam Muhammad in al-Jami' al-Saghir reported Abu Yusuf's view only for Umrah, not for Hajj, leading some to claim consensus (ittifaq) for Hajj. However, the correct position (asahh) is that it is disputed (mukhtalaf fih). The evidence (dalil) is then detailed. Abu Yusuf relies on the incident of Hudaybiyya where the Prophet (ﷺ) and his Companions shaved outside the Haram, proving that halq is not specific to the Haram. The two sides (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) analogize halq to the salam (taslim) in prayer: both are wajibat that also exit the ritual; since all manasik (rituals) of Hajj are specific to the Haram (like dhabh/slaughter), halq must also be specific. They respond to Abu Yusuf by noting that part of Hudaybiyya may be inside the Haram, so the incident does not prove permissibility outside. The text then delineates the four positions within the Hanafi school: Imam Abu Hanifa: halq is restricted by both time (days of Nahr) and place (Haram); Imam Abu Yusuf: not restricted by either; Imam Muhammad: restricted by place only; Imam Zufar: restricted by time only. Importantly, this ikhtilaf only concerns the obligation of dam (compensation). There is consensus that halq anywhere and any time exits ihram (makes one halal). Thus the practical difference is whether a dam must be offered. The commentary (tafseer) clarifies that the original matn discussed two cases: a haji shaving outside Haram during Hajj, and a person performing Umrah and trimming outside Haram. Both are subject to the same ikhtilaf. The author concludes that the mu'tamad (relied upon) view is that this is a valid ikhtilaf, and each position should be followed according to taqlid.

Key Terms
حلق (halq): Shaving the head completely, one of the wajibat of Hajj and Umrah that exits ihram.
قصر (qasr): Trimming the hair short, an alternative to halq for exiting ihram.
دم (dam): A sacrificial animal (sheep or goat) required as compensation for leaving a wajib or committing a prohibited act during Hajj/Umrah.
موقت (muwaqqat): Restricted or specified by a particular time or place; having a fixed time or location for validity.
توقیت (tawqit): The act of specifying a time or place for a ritual act.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, if a pilgrim shaves his head inside the Haram but after the days of Nahr (e.g., on the 13th of Dhul Hijjah), what is the ruling?
A) No dam is required because he shaved inside the Haram.
B) A dam is required because he missed the time (days of Nahr).
C) His Hajj is invalid because he shaved at the wrong time.
D) He must repeat the shaving on the correct day.

Key Takeaway
The obligation of dam for halq outside the Haram depends on whether halq is considered muwaqqat by time and place, a point on which the four Hanafi imams differ, but all agree that halq anywhere exits ihram.

Hajj — Pilgrimage
beginner
5 min
Halq and Qasr in Umrah: Not Time-Bound but Place-Bound
Consensus rule that halq/qasr in Umrah is not time-bound but is place-bound

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the time and place restrictions for halq and qasr in Umrah and apply it to determine the validity of performing these acts at different times and locations.

Core Idea
Halq/qasr in Umrah is not time-bound but is place-bound—must be within the Haram.

In this lesson, we derive a straightforward but fundamental rule from the Hanafi school: the acts of shaving (halq) or trimming (qasr) that conclude an Umrah are not restricted to any specific time. Unlike Hajj, where these acts are tied to the days of Nahr, Umrah can be performed at any moment—day or night, any month. However, there is one essential restriction: place. Both halq and qasr must be performed within the sacred precincts of the Haram in Makkah. This ruling, stated by al-Quduri and affirmed by consensus (ijma'), highlights the distinct nature of Umrah as a timeless act of worship, while emphasizing the sanctity of the Haram.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is halq (shaving) and qasr (trimming) performed in the context of Umrah. The ruling stated is that these acts are not muwaqqat bil-zaman (time-bound) by consensus.
The consensus (ijma') indicates no dispute among Hanafi scholars on this point.
2
Note the contrast with place
The text explicitly says 'khilaf al-makan' (contrary to place), indicating that while time is not a restriction, place is. Umrah is muwaqqat bihi (restricted by place), meaning halq/qasr must be done within the Haram.
The Haram refers to the sacred boundary around Makkah, including the Masjid al-Haram.
3
Understand the reasoning
Umrah itself is not time-bound because its essential components—tawaf and sa'i—are not tied to specific months or days. Therefore, the acts that complete Umrah follow the same rule.
This contrasts with Hajj, which is restricted to the months of Shawwal, Dhul-Qa'dah, and the first ten days of Dhul-Hijjah.
4
Recognize the consensus
The ruling is reported bil-ijma' (by consensus), meaning there is no intra-Hanafi or inter-madhhab disagreement on this point. It is a settled rule.
This strengthens the authority of the ruling.
5
Apply the rule to a scenario
If someone performs Umrah on any day of the year and shaves or trims their hair within the Haram, the act is valid regardless of the time. If they do it outside the Haram, they must pay dam (compensation).
The place restriction applies; time does not.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
حلق اور قصر عمرہ میں موقت بالزمان نہیں
وَالتَّقْصِيرُ وَ الْحَلْقُ فِي الْعُمَرَةِ غَيْرُ مُوَفَّتِ بِالزَّمَانِ بِالْإِجْمَاعِ لِأَنَّ أَصْلَ الْعُمْرَةِ لَا يُتَوَفَّتُ بِهِ بِخِلَافِ الْمَكَانِ لِأَنَّهُ مُوَفَّتٌ بِهِ
ترجمہ: اور عمرہ میں حلق اور قصر کرنا بالاجماع زمانہ کے ساتھ مختص نہیں ہے کیونکہ عمرہ خود کسی زمانہ کے ساتھ مختص نہیں ہے برخلاف مکان (حرم) کے کیونکہ عمرہ اس کے ساتھ موقت ہے۔
تشریح: صاحب قدوری فرماتے ہیں کہ عمرہ کے اندر حلق یا قصر کرنا کسی زمانہ کے ساتھ خاص نہیں ہے بلکہ جس زمانہ میں کرے گا بلا اختلاف درست ہوگا۔ کیونکہ عمرہ خود کسی زمانہ کے ساتھ مختص نہیں ہے بلکہ جس زمانہ میں چاہے عمرہ کرے کیونکہ عمرہ نام ہے طواف اور سعی کا۔
Halq and qasr in Umrah: Not restricted by time. And trimming and shaving in Umrah are not restricted by time by consensus, because the origin of Umrah itself is not restricted by time, unlike the place (Haram) because it is restricted by it. Translation: And in Umrah, shaving and trimming are not specific to any time by consensus, because Umrah itself is not specific to any time, contrary to place (Haram) because Umrah is restricted to it. Commentary: Sahib al-Quduri says that shaving or trimming in Umrah is not specific to any time; rather, whenever one does it, it is valid without dispute. Because Umrah itself is not specific to any time; rather, one may perform Umrah in any time, for Umrah is the name of tawaf and sa'i.
Source pages p. 448

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah quoting al-Quduri presents a clear ruling (hukm) regarding the timing of halq (shaving) and qasr (trimming) in Umrah. The matn states that these acts are not muwaqqat (restricted/specified) by time by consensus (ijma'). The reason given is that Umrah itself is not time-bound—it can be performed at any time of the year, unlike Hajj which has specific days. However, there is a contrast (khilaf) with place: Umrah is restricted by place (makan), meaning that the acts of halq and qasr must be performed within the boundaries of the Haram (the sacred precinct of Makkah). The commentary by Sahib al-Quduri confirms that there is no dispute (bila ikhtilaf) that these acts are valid regardless of when they are done, as long as they are done in the Haram. The reasoning is that Umrah essentially consists of tawaf (circumambulation) and sa'i (running between Safa and Marwah), which are not tied to specific days. This ruling stands in contrast to Hajj, where halq is restricted to the days of Nahr and the Haram, as discussed in the previous lesson. The consensus mentioned here is among the Hanafi imams and indeed across the major schools.

Key Terms
عمرہ (umrah): The lesser pilgrimage consisting of ihram, tawaf, sa'i, and halq/qasr; can be performed at any time of the year.
موقت بالزمان (muwaqqat bil-zaman): Restricted by time; having a specific time frame within which an act must be performed for validity.
اجماع (ijma'): Consensus of the scholars; here it refers to the agreement of the Hanafi school that halq/qasr in Umrah is not time-bound.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on performing halq (shaving) in Umrah during the month of Ramadan?
A) It is invalid because Umrah should not be done in Ramadan.
B) It is valid only if done on specific days of Ramadan.
C) It is valid at any time because halq/qasr in Umrah is not time-bound.
D) It is valid only if done after tawaf and sa'i, but the time of day matters.

Key Takeaway
Halq and qasr in Umrah are not time-specific but must be performed within the Haram.
